ام ولد اور مد بر مشتری کے ہاتھ میں ہلاک ہو جائیں تو مشتری پر ضمان ہے یا نہیں
قال وان ماتت ام الولد او المدبر فى يد المشترى فلا ضمان عليه عند ابي حنيفة وقالا عليه قيمتها وهو فلاضمان رواية عنه لهما انه مقبوض بجهة البيع فيكون مضموناً عليه كسائر الاموال وهذا لان المدبروام الولديد خلان تحت البيع حتى يملك ما يضم اليهما فى البيع بخلاف المكاتب لا في يد نفسه فلا يتحقق في حقه القبض وهذا الضمان بالقبض وله ان جهة البيع الما تلحق بحقيقة في محمل يقبل الحقيقة وهما لا يقبلان حقيقة البيع فصارا كالمكاتب وليس دخولهما فى البيع في حق انفسهما وانما ذالك ليثبت حكم البيع فيما ضم اليهما فصار كمال المشترى لا يدخل فى حكم عقده بانفراده وانما يثبت حكم الدخول فيما ضمه اليه كذا هذا
ترجمہ اور اگرام ولد یامد بر مشتری کے قبضہ میں مر گیا تو امام ابوحنیفہ کے نزدیک اس پر منمان نہیں ہے اور صاحبین نے کہا کہ اس پر دونوں کی قیمت واجب ہوگی اور یہی امام صاحب سے بھی ایک روایت ہے۔ صاحبین کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ ام ولد اور مدبر میں سے ہر ایک بہت السبع مقبوض ہے۔ اسلئے مبیع اس کی ضمانت میں ہوگی۔ جیسا کہ دوسرے اموال کا حکم ہے اسلئے کہ مدبر اور ام ولد دونوں بیع کے تحت داخل ہو جاتے ہیں حتی کہ جو چیز ان کے ساتھ ملائی جائے وہ ان کی بیچ میں مشتری کی مملوک ہو جاتی ہے برخلاف مکاتب کے کیونکہ وہ اپنے ڈائی قبضہ میں ہے پس اس کے حق میں قبضہ متحقق نہ ہوگا حالانکہ یہ ضمان قبضہ ہی کی وجہ سے ہے۔ اور امام ابو حنیفہ کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ جہت بیع کو حقیقت بیچ کے ساتھ ایسے محل میں لاحق کیا جاتا ہے جو حقیقت بیع کو قبول کرتا ہو حالانکہ یہ دونوں حقیقت بیع کو قبول نہیں کرتے ہیں۔ پس یہ دونوں بھی مکاتب کے مانند ہو گئے اور ان کا بیع کے اندر دخول خود ان کی ذات کے حق میں
And if umm walad or mudabbar die in the buyer's hand, is there liability upon the buyer? He said: If umm walad or mudabbar die in the buyer's hand, there is no liability upon him according to Abu Hanifa. And they (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: upon him is her value, and it is also narrated from him (Abu Hanifa) that there is no liability. Their (Sahibayn) proof is that it is possessed by virtue of sale, so it becomes liable upon him like other wealth. This is because the mudabbar and umm walad are included under the sale such that the buyer owns whatever is appended to them in the sale, unlike the mukatab because he is in his own possession, so possession is not realized in his case, and this liability is due to possession. And his (Abu Hanifa's) proof is that the aspect of sale (jihah al-bay') is attached to the reality of sale only in a locus that accepts the reality of sale, and these two (umm walad and mudabbar) do not accept the reality of sale, so they become like the mukatab. And their inclusion in the sale is not in respect of their own selves; rather it is to establish the effect of sale regarding what is appended to them. So it is like the buyer's wealth does not enter the ruling of his contract by itself; rather the ruling of entry is only established for what is appended to it. This is the same.
Source pages p. 163

Commentary
This is an intra-Hanafi dispute concerning liability (dhaman) if an umm walad or mudabbar dies while in the possession of the buyer. The issue is whether the buyer must pay the value to the seller. Abu Hanifa holds that there is no liability, while the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) hold that the buyer must pay the value. There is also a narration from Abu Hanifa agreeing with the Sahibayn. The Sahibayn argue that these slaves are possessed by virtue of a sale contract (even if batil), and anything possessed via a sale contract is liable, similar to other goods. They note that umm walad and mudabbar are included within the sale to the extent that if something is appended to them (e.g., another slave sold together), the buyer owns that appended item. This shows they are under the sale. The mukatab is different because he has possession of himself, so no actual possession by the buyer. Abu Hanifa's reasoning is that the 'aspect of sale' (jihah al-bay') attaches only to something that genuinely accepts the reality of sale. Since umm walad and mudabbar cannot be validly sold (their sale is batil), they do not accept the reality of sale, thus they are like the mukatab in this respect. Their inclusion in the sale is only for the sake of the appended item, not for themselves. Consequently, no liability arises for the buyer if they die. The dispute hinges on whether the sale, though batil, can generate effects like liability. The relied-upon position is not explicitly stated here, but later Hanafi fatwa may align with the Sahibayn for practical purposes.

Key Terms
ضمان (dhaman): Liability to pay compensation (value) for an item that is in one's possession and is destroyed or dies.
بجهة البيع (bi jihah al-bay'): By virtue of being under a sale contract, i.e., the item is in the buyer's possession due to a sale agreement.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, if an umm walad dies in the buyer's possession after an invalid sale, what is the ruling?
A) The buyer must pay her value.
B) The buyer is not liable.
C) The buyer must return her to the seller.
D) The buyer is liable only if he knew she was umm walad.

Key Takeaway
Intra-Hanafi dispute on dhaman for umm walad/mudabbar turns on whether jihah al-bay' attaches to items that cannot be validly sold.

Mukatab's Consent Validates His Sale
Ruling on mukatab's consent making his sale valid with hadith proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling when a mukatab consents to his own sale and explain the evidence from the hadith of 'Aisha and Barira.

Core Idea
A mukatab's consent removes the impediment, making his sale sahih.

This lesson examines a nuanced ruling from al-Hidayah regarding the sale of a mukatab. While there are two transmissions within the Hanafi school, the preferred position is that the sale becomes permissible when the mukatab gives his consent. The basis for this ruling is the hadith of 'Aisha and Barira, which demonstrates the validity of such a transaction without prophetic objection.

Guided Path
1
Identify the subject and the issue
Determine who a mukatab is and why his sale is legally problematic. A mukatab is a slave under kitabah (manumission contract) with independence over his person.
The impediment is the mukatab's right over himself under the kitabah.
2
State the two transmissions
There are two riwayat: one prohibits the sale even with consent, the other permits it. Identify which is preferred (azhar).
Azhar is permissibility.
3
Understand the rationale
The sale was originally impermissible due to the mukatab's right. When he consents, he drops that right, rescinding the kitabah and making the sale valid.
Consent is not just permission but a waiver of right.
4
Examine the proof
The hadith: 'Aisha purchased Barira (a mukatabah) with her consent and freed her. The Prophet did not object, showing validity.
The wajh al-dalalah is that the action was tacitly approved.
5
Apply the ruling
In practice, if a mukatab consents to being sold to another master, the sale is sahih. If he does not consent, it remains invalid.
The mufta bihi is the permissibility view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ اگر مکاتب اپنی بیع پر خود راضی ہو گیا تو اس میں دور روایتیں ہیں ایک روایت عدم جواز کی ہے اور دوسری روایت جواز کی ہے۔ اظہر یہی ہے کیونکہ عدم جواز مکاتب کے حق کی وجہ سے تھا لیکن جب اس نے اپنی رضا مندی سے خود ہی اپنا حق ساقط کر دیا تو کتابت فسخ ہو کر بیع جائز ہو گئی۔ اس کی تائید صحیحین کی حدیث سے بھی ہوتی ہے کہ حضرت عائشہ نے بریرہ مکاتبہ کو اس کی رضا مندی سے خرید کر آزاد کیا تھا۔
The author of al-Hidayah says: If a mukatab consents to his own sale, then there are two transmissions: one transmission of impermissibility and the other transmission of permissibility. The more apparent is this (permissibility) because the impermissibility was due to the right of the mukatab, but when he dropped his right of his own consent, the kitabah is rescinded and the sale becomes permissible. This is also supported by the hadith in the two Sahihs that 'Aisha purchased Barira, who was a mukatabah, with her consent and freed her.'
Source pages p. 163

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling from al-Hidayah regarding the sale of a mukatab when he consents. The author explains that there are two narrations: one prohibiting it and one allowing it. The preferred (azhar) position is permissibility because the prohibition was originally due to the right of the mukatab over himself. When he voluntarily relinquishes that right, the contract of kitabah is cancelled, and the sale becomes valid. The proof is the hadith of 'Aisha buying Barira, a mukatabah, with her consent. This indicates that the sale of a mukatab with his consent is valid, as his right is his own to waive.

Key Terms
مکاتب (mukatab): A slave who has entered into a contract of kitabah (manumission by payment) with his master.
کتابت (kitabah): The contract between a master and a slave whereby the slave is to be freed upon payment of a sum.
اظہر (azhar): The more apparent or preferred opinion among conflicting narrations.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling when a mukatab consents to his own sale?
A) The sale is invalid because a mukatab cannot be sold under any circumstances.
B) The sale becomes permissible (jāʼiz) because the mukatab has dropped his right.
C) The sale is valid only if the master is in dire need.
D) The sale is valid only if the mukatab has not yet paid anything.

Key Takeaway
The sale of a mukatab becomes valid when he consents, as his right over himself is waived.

Sale of Mudabbar Mutlaq is Invalid: Hanafi vs Shafi'i
Inter-madhhab dispute on the sale of mudabbar mutlaq

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the sale of a mudabbar mutlaq, explain the Shafi'i counter-argument, and evaluate the Hanafi response based on the hadith evidence.

Core Idea
A mudabbar mutlaq cannot be sold because the hadith explicitly prohibits it.

This lesson examines a key inter-madhhab dispute in the fiqh of sales: whether a mudabbar (a slave whose freedom is tied to the master's death) can be sold while the master is alive. The Hanafi school holds that the mudabbar mutlaq (absolute tadbir) cannot be sold, gifted, or inherited, based on a Prophetic hadith. Imam al-Shafi'i, however, considers such a sale permissible, arguing that the suspending condition does not negate ownership. We will dissect the proofs and understand the practical consequences of this difference.

Guided Path
1
Distinguish the types of mudabbar
First, differentiate between mudabbar mutlaq (absolute, freedom tied solely to death) and mudabbar muqayyad (restricted, freedom tied to death plus another condition). The Hanafi ruling applies only to the former.
Mudabbar muqayyad can be sold by consensus.
2
State the Hanafi position and its proof
The Hanafi school rules that selling a mudabbar mutlaq is invalid (batil). Their evidence is the hadith: 'al-mudabbar la yuba' wa la yuhab wa la yurath' (the mudabbar is not sold, nor gifted, nor inherited).
The negation 'la' indicates prohibition.
3
Present the Shafi'i position and its proof
Imam al-Shafi'i holds the sale is valid. His argument: suspending freedom on a condition (like 'if you enter the house, you are free') does not prevent sale, because the master retains ownership until death. So selling a mudabbar mutlaq should be permissible by analogy.
The condition is a future contingency.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
The Hanafis respond that the explicit hadith overrides any analogy. Any alleged sale by the Prophet of a mudabbar is interpreted as a mudabbar muqayyad, which is permissible by agreement, not a mudabbar mutlaq.
The hadith is specific to mudabbar mutlaq.
5
Determine the practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf)
The consequence: In the Hanafi school, a sale of a mudabbar mutlaq is void, so the buyer gains no ownership and must return the slave. In the Shafi'i school, the sale is valid, and the mudabbar status transfers to the new owner, who then becomes the master with the same tadbir obligation.
This affects inheritance and gift as well.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
صاحب بدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ متن میں مدبر سے مرادید بر مطلق ہے یعنی مد بر مطلق کی بیع باطل ہے کیونکہ مد بر مقید کی بیع بالا تفاق جائز ہے البتہ حضرت امام شافعی نے مدبر مطلق کی بیع کو بھی جائزہ کہا ہے۔ امام شافعی کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ مد بر مطلق کی صورت میں غلام کی آزادی مولیٰ کی موت پر معلق کی گئی ہے اور آزادی کو کسی شرط پر معلق کرنا ( مثال) کہنا ان دخلت الدار فانت حر ) بیچ اور ہبہ کیلئے مانع نہیں ہے اسلئے مد بر مطلق یعنی غلام کی آزادی کو مولی کی مطلق موت پر معلق کرنے کی صورت میں بھی غلام کو بیچنا اور بہبہ کرنا جائز ہوگا۔ ہماری دلیل حدیث ہے المدير لا يباع ولا يوهب ولا يورث یعنی مدبر کو نہ فروخت کیا جائے گا اور نہ ہبہ کیا جائے گا اور نہ اس میں وراثت جاری ہوگی ۔ اس حدیث سے واضح طور پر ثابت ہے کہ مدبر کی بیچ نا جائز ہے اور اگر امام شافعی یہ فرمائیں کہ رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے مد بر فروخت کیا ہے تو اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ وہ مد بر مطلق نہ تھا بلکہ مد بر مقید تھا اور مدبر مقید کی بیع کے جواز کے ہم بھی قائل ہیں۔ اس کی تفصیل کتاب العتاق باب اللہ بیر میں ملاحظہ فرمائیں۔
The author of al-Bidayah says: In the text, mudabbar refers to mudabbar mutlaq (absolute), meaning the sale of a mudabbar mutlaq is invalid, because the sale of a mudabbar muqayyad (restricted) is permissible by agreement. However, Imam al-Shafi'i has said that the sale of a mudabbar mutlaq is also permissible. Imam al-Shafi'i's evidence is that in the case of a mudabbar mutlaq, the slave's freedom is suspended on the master's death, and suspending freedom on a condition (e.g., saying 'if you enter the house, you are free') is not a barrier to sale and gift. Therefore, in the case of a mudabbar mutlaq, i.e., suspending the slave's freedom on the absolute death of the master, selling and gifting the slave is also permissible. Our evidence is the hadith: 'al-mudabbar la yuba' wa la yuhab wa la yurath' meaning 'The mudabbar is not sold, nor given, nor inherited.' This hadith clearly establishes that selling a mudabbar is impermissible. And if Imam al-Shafi'i says that the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) sold a mudabbar, then the response is that it was not a mudabbar mutlaq but a mudabbar muqayyad, and we also believe in the permissibility of selling a mudabbar muqayyad. See the details in the book of 'itaq, chapter of al-mudabbar.
Source pages p. 163

Commentary
This passage discusses a key inter-madhhab dispute regarding the sale of a mudabbar. A mudabbar is a slave whose freedom is conditioned upon the master's death. There are two types: mudabbar mutlaq (where the freedom is tied solely to death) and mudabbar muqayyad (where it is tied to death with additional conditions, e.g., 'if I die from this illness, you are free'). The Hanafi position is that a mudabbar mutlaq cannot be sold at all, based on the hadith 'al-mudabbar la yuba' wa la yuhab wa la yurath'. Imam al-Shafi'i argues that since the slavery is still existent during the master's lifetime, and the condition (death) does not prevent sale, it should be permissible. The Hanafi response is that the hadith explicitly prohibits the sale, and any report that the Prophet sold a mudabbar refers to a mudabbar muqayyad, which is not subject to the prohibition. This dispute hinges on the interpretation of the hadith and the nature of the mudabbar's status.

Key Terms
مدبر (mudabbar): A slave whose freedom is suspended upon the death of his master.
مدبر مطلق (mudabbar mutlaq): A mudabbar whose freedom is solely tied to the master's death without additional conditions.
مدبر مقید (mudabbar muqayyad): A mudabbar whose freedom is tied to the master's death but with additional restrictions or conditions.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Mudabbar muqayyad
B) Mudabbar mutlaq
C) Both types
D) Neither type

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school prohibits the sale of a mudabbar mutlaq due to an explicit hadith, while the Shafi'i school allows it by analogy; the core distinction is between absolute and restricted tadbir.

Daman for Umm Walad and Mudabbar: Abu Hanifa vs Sahibayn
Intra-Hanafi dispute on daman for umm walad and mudabbar

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa and Sahibayn regarding daman for umm walad and mudabbar, and explain the reasoning behind each position, including the correction of narrations from Hidayah.

Core Idea
Possession by virtue of sale triggers liability, but only if the object accepts the haqiqa of sale — umm walad and mudabbar do not, so no daman.

When a slave with special status (umm walad or mudabbar) is sold together with another slave and then dies in the buyer's possession, is the buyer liable for its value? The Hanafi school has a well-known disagreement: Abu Hanifa holds no liability, while Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (Sahibayn) hold the buyer must pay. This lesson unpacks the legal reasoning and clarifies a common misunderstanding about the narrations from Abu Hanifa.

Guided Path
1
Identify the disputed ruling
The dispute is about daman (liability) when an umm walad or mudabbar dies in the buyer's possession after a sale. State the two positions: Abu Hanifa says no daman; Sahibayn say daman with value.
Note that for mudabbar, there is also a riwaya from Abu Hanifa supporting Sahibayn.
2
Analyze Sahibayn's proof
Sahibayn argue that both umm walad and mudabbar fall under the contract of sale (as evidenced by the buyer owning a slave sold together with them). Therefore, possession is 'bi-jahati al-bay'' (by virtue of sale), which triggers daman.
They compare to regular property: any item possessed by virtue of a sale is guaranteed.
3
Analyze Abu Hanifa's proof
Abu Hanifa argues that umm walad and mudabbar do not accept the haqiqa (reality) of sale because they have rights to freedom (umm walad free on master's death; mudabbar on a condition). Thus, their inclusion in the sale is only to facilitate sale of another slave, not to make them fully subject to sale. Hence possession is not truly 'bi-jahati al-bay''.
He analogizes them to a mukatib, who also does not accept the haqiqa.
4
Examine the exception of mukatib
Sahibayn have an exception: a mukatib does not trigger daman because his possession is in his own hand; the buyer's possession is not realized. Abu Hanifa uses this to argue that umm walad and mudabbar are similar.
This shows that daman depends on actual possession, not merely entry under contract.
5
Correct the narration misunderstanding
The passage clarifies that Hidayah's wording might imply two narrations from Abu Hanifa for both, but in reality: for mudabbar there are two narrations (no daman and daman), while for umm walad all narrations agree on no daman.
This correction is important for proper fiqh application.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ام ولد اور مد بر مشتری کے ہاتھ میں ہلاک ہو جائیں تو مشتری پر ضمان ہے یا نہیں
قال وان ماتت ام الولد او المدبر فى يد المشترى فلا ضمان عليه عند ابي حنيفة وقالا عليه قيمتها وهو فلاضمان رواية عنه لهما انه مقبوض بجهة البيع فيكون مضموناً عليه كسائر الاموال وهذا لان المدبروام الولديد خلان تحت البيع حتى يملك ما يضم اليهما فى البيع بخلاف المكاتب لا في يد نفسه فلا يتحقق في حقه القبض وهذا الضمان بالقبض وله ان جهة البيع الما تلحق بحقيقة في محمل يقبل الحقيقة وهما لا يقبلان حقيقة البيع فصارا كالمكاتب وليس دخولهما فى البيع في حق انفسهما وانما ذالك ليثبت حكم البيع فيما ضم اليهما فصار كمال المشترى لا يدخل فى حكم عقده بانفراده وانما يثبت حكم الدخول فيما ضمه اليه كذا هذا
ترجمہ اور اگرام ولد یامد بر مشتری کے قبضہ میں مر گیا تو امام ابوحنیفہ کے نزدیک اس پر منمان نہیں ہے اور صاحبین نے کہا کہ اس پر دونوں کی قیمت واجب ہوگی اور یہی امام صاحب سے بھی ایک روایت ہے۔ صاحبین کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ ام ولد اور مدبر میں سے ہر ایک بہت السبع مقبوض ہے۔ اسلئے مبیع اس کی ضمانت میں ہوگی۔ جیسا کہ دوسرے اموال کا حکم ہے اسلئے کہ مدبر اور ام ولد دونوں بیع کے تحت داخل ہو جاتے ہیں حتی کہ جو چیز ان کے ساتھ ملائی جائے وہ ان کی بیچ میں مشتری کی مملوک ہو جاتی ہے برخلاف مکاتب کے کیونکہ وہ اپنے ڈائی قبضہ میں ہے پس اس کے حق میں قبضہ متحقق نہ ہوگا حالانکہ یہ ضمان قبضہ ہی کی وجہ سے ہے۔ اور امام ابو حنیفہ کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ جہت بیع کو حقیقت بیچ کے ساتھ ایسے محل میں لاحق کیا جاتا ہے جو حقیقت بیع کو قبول کرتا ہو حالانکہ یہ دونوں حقیقت بیع کو قبول نہیں کرتے ہیں۔ پس یہ دونوں بھی مکاتب کے مانند ہو گئے اور ان کا بیع کے اندر دخول خود ان کی ذات کے حق میں
نہیں ہے بلکہ صرف اسلئے ہے تا کہ ان کے ساتھ ملائی ہوئی چیز میں بیچ کا حکم ثابت ہو جائے ۔ پس ایسا ہو گیا جیسا کہ مشتری کا مال اس کی پیج کے حکم میں تنہا داخل نہیں ہوتا ہے بلکہ داخل ہونے کا حکم صرف اس مال میں ثابت ہوتا ہے جس کو بائع نے مشتری کے مال کے ساتھ ملانیا ہے۔ یہی حکم مد بر اورام ولد میں ہے۔
تشریح صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ ام ولد یا مد براگر مشتری کے قبضہ میں مرجائے تو حضرت امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک مشتری پر کوئی ضمان واجب نہ ہوگا اور صاحبین کے نزدیک مشتری پر قیمت کے ساتھ ضمان واجب ہوگا یہی ایک روایت امام ابو حنیفہ سے ہے۔ ہدایہ کی عبارت سے ظاہر ہوتا ہے کہ مدبر اور ام ولد دونوں میں امام صاحب سے دو روایتیں ہیں۔ ایک روایت عدم وجوب ضمان کی اور ایک وجوب عنمان کی ۔ حالانکہ یہ غلط ہے بلکہ صحیح یہ ہے کہ حضرت امام ابو حنیفہ سے مدبر کے حق میں دو روایتیں ہیں یعنی اگر مشتری کے قبضہ میں مدبر مر گیا تو امام صاحب کی ایک روایت یہ ہے کہ مشتری پر ضمان واجب نہ ہوگا اور دوسری روایت یہ ہے کہ ضمان بالقیمت واجب ہوگا اور ام ولد کے حق میں حضرت امام ابوحنیفہ سے تمام روایات عدم وجوب ضمان پر متفق ہیں یعنی اگر مشتری کے قبضہ میں ام ولد مرگئی تو امام صاحب سے صرف یہ روایت ہے کہ مشتری پر عمان واجب نہ ہوگا۔
صاحبین کی دلیل یہ ہےکہ مدبر اورام ولد پر مشتری کا قبضہ بہت البیع ہوتا ہے اور بہت البیع قبضہ اسلئے ہوتا ہے کہ مد بر اورام ولد دونوں عقد بیع کے تحت داخل ہو جاتے ہیں۔ یہی وجہ ہے کہ مدبر اور ام ولد کے ساتھ اگر کوئی غلام ملا کر فروخت کیا گیا تو مشتری اس غلام کا اس کے حصہ ثمن کے عوض مالک ہو جاتا ہے۔ اگر مد بر اورام ولد عقد بیع کے تحت داخل نہ ہوتے تو جو غلام ان کے ساتھ ملا کر فروخت کیا گیا ہے۔ مشتری اس کا مالک ہرگز نہ ہوتا جیسے اگر کوئی آزاد آدمی اور غلام کو ملا کر فروخت کر دے تو مشتری غلام کا مالک نہیں ہوتا۔ کیونکہ آزاد آدمی جس کے ساتھ ملا کر غلام فروخت کیا گیا ہے وہ عقد بیع کے تحت داخل نہیں ہوتا۔ بہر حال یہ بات ثابت ہوگئی کہ مد بر اورام ولد عقد بیع کے تحت داخل ہوتے ہیں اور جو چیز عقد بیع کے تحت داخل ہوتی ہے۔ اس پر مشترکی کا قبضہ بہت البیع ہوتا ہے اور مقبوض بہت البيع مضمون ہوتا ہے یعنی ہلاکت کی صورت میں قابض پر ضمان واجب ہوتا ہے۔ جیسا کہ دوسرے اموال ، مقبوض علی سوم الشراء کی صورت میں مضمون ہوتے ہیں۔ اگر مد بریا ام ولد مشتری کے قبضہ میں مرجائے تو مشتری پر اس کا ضمان واجب ہو گا۔ بخلاف المکاتب سے صاحبین کی طرف سے سوال کا جواب ہے۔ سوال یہ ہے کہ اگر کسی چیز کا عقد بیع کے تحت داخل ہونا اور جو چیز اس کے ساتھ ملا کر فروخت کی گئی ہے۔ اس پر مشتری کی ملکیت کا ثابت ہونا منمان واجب ہونے کا سبب ہے تو مکاتب کے حق میں بھی یہ بات ہونی چاہئے تھی کہ مکاتب اگر مشتری کے قبضہ میں مرجائے تو مشتری پر اس کا منعمان واجب ہو، کیونکہ مکاتب عقد بیع کے تحت بھی داخل ہوتا ہے اور اگر غلام اس کے ساتھ ملا کر بیچا جائے تو مشتری اس غلام کا اس کے حصہ ثمن کے عوض مالک بھی ہو جاتا ہے۔ حالانکہ مکاتب اگر مشتری کے قبضہ میں مر جائے تو صاحبین کے نزدیک مشتری پر مکاتب کا ضمان واجب نہیں ہوتا۔ ایسا کیوں ہے؟ اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ مکاتب کا قبضہ ہی اپنی ذات پر چونکہ خود ہوتا ہے۔ اسلئے اس کے حق میں مشتری کا قبضہ متفق نہ ہوگا ۔ حالانکہ یہ ضمان قبضہ ہی کی وجہ سے واجب ہوتا ہے۔ پس جب مکاتب پر مشتری کا قبضہ ہی متحقق نہ ہوا تو مشتری پر اس کا ضمان بھی واجب نہ ہوگا۔ حاصل یہ کہ وجوب ضمان کا مدار مشتری کا قبضہ ہے نہ عقد کے تحت داخل ہونا ہے اور نہ اس چیز کا مالک ہوتا ہے جس کو اسکے ساتھ ملا کر فروخت کیا ہے۔ پس جب مدار ضمان یعنی قبضہ نہیں پایا گیا تو مشتری پر مکاتب کا ضمان بھی واجب نہ ہوگا۔
If the umm walad or mudabbar dies in the hand of the buyer, then according to Abu Hanifa there is no daman on him, and the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: on him is their value. And this is a riwaya from him (Abu Hanifa) as well. For them (the two), it is received by virtue of the sale (bi-jahati al-bay'), so it is guaranteed (mazmun) upon him like other properties. This is because the mudabbar and umm walad both fall under the contract of sale to the extent that what is combined with them in the sale becomes owned (by the buyer). Unlike the mukatib, who is in his own hand, so for him possession (qabd) is not realized. And this daman is due to qabd. For him (Abu Hanifa), the aspect (jahat) of sale attaches to a reality (haqiqa) in a mahall (locus) that accepts the haqiqa, and they (mudabbar and umm walad) do not accept the haqiqa of sale, so they become like the mukatib. Their inclusion in the sale is not for themselves but only to establish the ruling of sale in what is combined with them. So it is like the buyer's property does not enter into the ruling of his contract alone, but rather the ruling of entry is established only in what he combines with it. Similarly here. Translation (Urdu): And if the umm walad or mudabbar dies in the possession of the buyer, then according to Imam Abu Hanifa, no daman is due; and Sahibayn said that the value of both becomes wajib upon him, and this is also a narration from Imam (Abu Hanifa). The proof of Sahibayn is that each of umm walad and mudabbar is maqbood bi-jahati al-bay', therefore the sold item is in his dhaman, like the ruling of other properties. This is because both mudabbar and umm walad enter under the contract of sale, such that what is mixed with them becomes owned by the buyer. Unlike the mukatib, because he is in his own possession, so qabd is not realized for him, while this daman is due to qabd. And the proof of Imam Abu Hanifa is that the jahat of sale attaches to the haqiqa of sale in a mahall that accepts the haqiqa, and these two do not accept the haqiqa of sale. So they become like the mukatib. Their inclusion in the sale is not for themselves but only to establish the ruling of sale in what is combined with them. So it becomes like the buyer's property does not enter the ruling of his contract alone, but the ruling of entry is only established in what he combines with it. This is the same ruling for mudabbar and umm walad. Tashreeh: The image of the issue is that if umm walad or mudabbar dies in the buyer's possession, then according to Imam Abu Hanifa, no daman is wajib on the buyer, and according to Sahibayn, daman with value is wajib on the buyer. This is also one narration from Imam Abu Hanifa. From the phrase of Hidayah, it appears that regarding both mudabbar and umm walad, there are two narrations from Imam: one of non-obligation of daman and one of obligation. However, this is incorrect. Rather, the correct is that from Imam Abu Hanifa regarding mudabbar there are two narrations: if mudabbar dies in the buyer's possession, one narration says no daman is wajib, and another says daman with value is wajib. And regarding umm walad, all narrations from Imam Abu Hanifa agree on non-obligation of daman: i.e., if umm walad dies in the buyer's possession, only the narration that no daman is wajib is reported. The proof of Sahibayn is that the buyer's possession over mudabbar and umm walad is bi-jahati al-bay', and it is bi-jahati al-bay' because both mudabbar and umm walad enter under the contract of sale. This is the reason that if a slave is sold mixed with them, the buyer owns that slave for his share of the price. If they did not enter under the contract of sale, then the slave sold mixed with them would not be owned by the buyer, just as if a free man and a slave are sold together, the buyer does not own the slave. Because the free man with whom the slave is sold does not enter under the contract of sale. So it is established that mudabbar and umm walad enter under the contract of sale, and whatever enters under the contract of sale, the buyer's possession over it is bi-jahati al-bay', and maqbood bi-jahati al-bay' is mazmun, meaning that if it perishes, the possessor is liable for daman. Just as other properties, when received on the basis of purchase, are mazmun. So if mudabbar or umm walad dies in the buyer's possession, the buyer is liable for its daman. As for the exception of the mukatib, this is the answer to a question from Sahibayn. The question is: if something's entering under the contract of sale and the buyer's ownership over what is sold with it is the cause of daman, then the same should apply to the mukatib: if the mukatib dies in the buyer's possession, the buyer should be liable for his daman, because the mukatib also enters under the contract of sale, and if a slave is sold with him, the buyer owns that slave for his share of the price. Yet, if the mukatib dies in the buyer's possession, according to Sahibayn, the buyer is not liable for daman. Why? The answer is: because the mukatib's possession is over himself, so the buyer's possession over him is not realized, while this daman is wajib due to possession. So when the buyer's possession over the mukatib is not realized, daman is not wajib on him. The conclusion is that the basis for the obligation of daman is the buyer's possession, not entering under the contract, nor ownership of what is sold with it. So when the basis of daman, i.e., possession, is not found, then the buyer's daman for the mukatib is not wajib.
Source pages p. 163

Commentary
This passage discusses an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding whether the buyer is liable (daman) when an umm walad (slave mother of the master's child) or a mudabbar dies in his possession after being sold along with another slave. The text clarifies that according to Imam Abu Hanifa, no daman is due, while Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (Sahibayn) hold that the buyer must pay the value. An additional narration from Abu Hanifa also supports Sahibayn's view for the mudabbar, but for umm walad, all narrations from Abu Hanifa agree on no daman. The reasoning revolves around whether these individuals are truly subject to the haqiqa (reality) of a sale contract. Sahibayn argue that because umm walad and mudabbar fall under the contract of sale (as evidenced by the ruling that if another slave is sold with them, the buyer owns that slave), the buyer's possession over them is by virtue of the sale (bi-jahati al-bay'), making them guaranteed. Abu Hanifa argues that these individuals do not accept the haqiqa of a sale (since they have rights to freedom, etc.), so they are like a mukatib (who also does not accept the haqiqa). The inclusion of umm walad and mudabbar in the sale is only to facilitate the sale of an accompanying slave, not to make them themselves fully subject to sale. Therefore, possession over them is not truly by virtue of sale, and thus no daman arises. The text then clarifies a common mistake from Hidayah's wording, noting that for mudabbar there are indeed two narrations from Abu Hanifa, but for umm walad all narrations agree on no daman. Finally, it addresses an objection: if entry under the contract causes daman, then why isn't a mukatib subject to daman? The answer is that the mukatib has possession of himself, so the buyer's possession is not realized, and daman is based on possession, not merely on entry under the contract.

Key Terms
ام ولد (umm walad): A female slave who has borne a child to her master, and thereby becomes free upon her master's death.
مدبر (mudabbar): A slave whose freedom is conditional on the master's death.
ضمان (daman): Liability to pay compensation in case of loss or destruction.
بہت البیع (bi-jahati al-bay'): By virtue of the sale; used to describe possession that is the result of a valid sale contract.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the corrected understanding of narrations, how many narrations are there from Imam Abu Hanifa regarding daman for umm walad?
A) Two: one for no daman, one for daman.
B) Only one: no daman.
C) Only one: daman with value.
D) None; Abu Hanifa did not express a view.

Key Takeaway
For umm walad, the Hanafi school (based on all narrations from Abu Hanifa) holds no daman; for mudabbar, there is a disagreement between Abu Hanifa and Sahibayn, with a riwaya from Abu Hanifa supporting Sahibayn.

Buyu — Sales and Trade
intermediate
10 min
The Ruling on Guarantee for Mudabbar and Umm Walad Sold Mixed
Intra-Hanafi dispute on daman

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi positions (Abu Hanifa vs. Sahibayn) on whether guarantee (daman) is obligatory when a mudabbar or umm walad dies in the buyer's possession after a mixed sale, and identify the operative ruling (mufta bihi).

Core Idea
A mudabbar or umm walad enters the sale only to validate the mixed property, not for itself—Sahibayn disagree, and the mufta bihi follows them.

This lesson examines an intra-Hanafi dispute concerning the guarantee (daman) of special slaves—mudabbar and umm walad—when they are sold mixed with another slave and then die in the buyer's possession. The disagreement between Imam Abu Hanifa and the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) turns on whether these slaves truly enter the sale contract. Understanding this dispute sharpens your ability to identify the operative ruling (mufta bihi) in Hanafi fiqh.

Guided Path
1
State the dispute scenario
A mudabbar or umm walad is sold mixed with another slave. The buyer takes possession. The slave dies in the buyer's possession. Is the buyer liable for its value?
2
Identify Imam Abu Hanifa's position
According to Abu Hanifa, no guarantee is obligatory on the buyer. For mudabbar, there is a second narration that guarantee is obligatory, but for umm walad all narrations agree on no guarantee.
3
Identify the Sahibayn's position
According to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, guarantee is obligatory on the buyer for both mudabbar and umm walad.
4
Apply the tarjih
The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position is that of the Sahibayn: guarantee is obligatory.
5
Note the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
The buyer must pay the price if the slave dies unless he can prove an exemption, according to Sahibayn; according to Abu Hanifa, the buyer bears no loss.

اگر مشتری کے قبضہ میں مدبر مر گیا تو امام صاحب کی ایک روایت یہ ہے کہ مشتری پر ضمان واجب نہ ہوگا اور دوسری روایت یہ ہے کہ ضمان بالقیمت واجب ہوگا اور ام ولد کے حق میں حضرت امام ابوحنیفہ سے تمام روایات عدم وجوب ضمان پر متفق ہیں یعنی اگر مشتری کے قبضہ میں ام ولد مرگئی تو امام صاحب سے صرف یہ روایت ہے کہ مشتری پر ضمان واجب نہ ہوگا۔ صاحبین کی دلیل یہ ہےکہ مدبر اورام ولد پر مشتری کا قبضہ بہت البیع ہوتا ہے اور بہت البیع قبضہ اسلئے ہوتا ہے کہ مد بر اورام ولد دونوں عقد بیع کے تحت داخل ہو جاتے ہیں۔ یہی وجہ ہے کہ مدبر اور ام ولد کے ساتھ اگر کوئی غلام ملا کر فروخت کیا گیا تو مشتری اس غلام کا اس کے حصہ ثمن کے عوض مالک ہو جاتا ہے۔ اگر مد بر اورام ولد عقد بیع کے تحت داخل نہ ہوتے تو جو غلام ان کے ساتھ ملا کر فروخت کیا گیا ہے۔ مشتری اس کا مالک ہرگز نہ ہوتا جیسے اگر کوئی آزاد آدمی اور غلام کو ملا کر فروخت کر دے تو مشتری غلام کا مالک نہیں ہوتا۔ کیونکہ آزاد آدمی جس کے ساتھ ملا کر غلام فروخت کیا گیا ہے وہ عقد بیع کے تحت داخل نہیں ہوتا۔ بہر حال یہ بات ثابت ہوگئی کہ مد بر اورام ولد عقد بیع کے تحت داخل ہوتے ہیں اور جو چیز عقد بیع کے تحت داخل ہوتی ہے۔ اس پر مشتری کا قبضہ بہت البیع ہوتا ہے اور مقبوض بہت البيع مضمون ہوتا ہے یعنی ہلاکت کی صورت میں قابض پر ضمان واجب ہوتا ہے۔ جیسا کہ دوسرے اموال ، مقبوض علی سوم الشراء کی صورت میں مضمون ہوتے ہیں۔ اگر مد بریا ام ولد مشتری کے قبضہ میں مرجائے تو مشتری پر اس کا ضمان واجب ہو گا۔ بخلاف المکاتب سے صاحبین کی طرف سے سوال کا جواب ہے۔ سوال یہ ہے کہ اگر کسی چیز کا عقد بیع کے تحت داخل ہونا اور جو چیز اس کے ساتھ ملا کر فروخت کی گئی ہے۔ اس پر مشتری کی ملکیت کا ثابت ہونا ضمان واجب ہونے کا سبب ہے تو مکاتب کے حق میں بھی یہ بات ہونی چاہئے تھی کہ مکاتب اگر مشتری کے قبضہ میں مرجائے تو مشتری پر اس کا ضمان واجب ہو، کیونکہ مکاتب عقد بیع کے تحت بھی داخل ہوتا ہے اور اگر غلام اس کے ساتھ ملا کر بیچا جائے تو مشتری اس غلام کا اس کے حصہ ثمن کے عوض مالک بھی ہو جاتا ہے۔ حالانکہ مکاتب اگر مشتری کے قبضہ میں مر جائے تو صاحبین کے نزدیک مشتری پر مکاتب کا ضمان واجب نہیں ہوتا۔ ایسا کیوں ہے؟ اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ مکاتب کا قبضہ ہی اپنی ذات پر چونکہ خود ہوتا ہے۔ اسلئے اس کے حق میں مشتری کا قبضہ متحقق نہ ہوگا ۔ حالانکہ یہ ضمان قبضہ ہی کی وجہ سے واجب ہوتا ہے۔ پس جب مکاتب پر مشتری کا قبضہ ہی متحقق نہ ہوا تو مشتری پر اس کا ضمان بھی واجب نہ ہوگا۔ حاصل یہ کہ وجوب ضمان کا مدار مشتری کا قبضہ ہے نہ عقد کے تحت داخل ہونا ہے اور نہ اس چیز کا مالک ہوتا ہے جس کو اسکے ساتھ ملا کر فروخت کیا ہے۔ پس جب مدار ضمان یعنی قبضہ نہیں پایا گیا تو مشتری پر مکاتب کا ضمان بھی واجب نہ ہوگا۔ حضرت امام ابو حنیفہ کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ جہت بیع ان اموال میں موجب ضمان ہے جن اموال میں جہت بیع کو حقیقت بیع کے ساتھ لاحق کیا جا سکتا ہو اور جہت بیع کو حقیقت بیع کے ساتھ ان اموال میں لاحق کیا جاتا ہے جو اموال حقیقت بیع کو قبول کرتے ہوں۔ اور مدبر اور ام ولد چونکہ مکاتب کی طرح حقیقت بیع کو قبول نہیں کرتے اسلئے ان کے حق میں جہت بیع کو حقیقت بیع کے ساتھ لاحق نہیں کیا جا سکتا ہے اور جب ان کے حق میں جہت بیع کو حقیقت بیع کے ساتھ لاحق نہیں کیا جا سکتا تو جہت بیع موجب ضمان بھی نہ ہوگی۔ اور جب جہت بیع موجب ضمان نہیں تو مدبر اور ام ولد اگر مشتری کے قبضہ میں مرجائیں تو مشتری پر ان کا ضمان واجب نہ ہوگا۔ وليس دخولهما في البيع سے صاحبین کی دلیل کا جواب ہے۔ جواب کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ مد بر اور ام ولد چونکہ بیع کا محل نہیں ہیں۔ اسلئے یہ دونوں خود اپنی ذات کے حق میں عقد بیع کے تحت داخل نہیں ہوتے ہیں بلکہ صرف اسلئے بیع کے تحت داخل ہوتے ہیں تا کہ جو چیز یعنی غلام وغیرہ ان کے ساتھ ملا کر فروخت کی گئی ہے اس میں بیع کا حکم یعنی مشتری کی ملکیت ثابت ہو جائے اور ایسا ہونا مستبعد نہیں ہے بلکہ شریعت میں اس کی نظیر موجود ہے۔ چنانچہ اگر کسی نے اپنا غلام اور خالد کا غلام ملا کر خالد کے ہاتھ فروخت کر دیا تو خالد بائع کے غلام کا اس کے حصہ ثمن کے عوض مالک ہو جاتا ہے۔ پس بائع کے غلام کے حق میں عقد بیع درست ہو گیا اور مشتری یعنی خالد کا غلام عقد بیع کے تحت خود اپنی ذات کے حق میں اگر چہ داخل نہیں ہوا لیکن بائع کے غلام میں حکم بیع یعنی مشتری کی ملک ثابت کرنے کیلئے بیع کے تحت داخل ہو گیا ہے۔ اسی طرح یہاں مدبر اور ام ولد اگر چہ خود اپنی ذات کے حق میں عقد بیع کے تحت داخل نہیں ہوئے لیکن جو غلام ان کے ساتھ ملا کر بیچا گیا ہے اس کے اندر مشتری کی ملک ثابت کرنے کیلئے عقد بیع کے تحت داخل ہو گئے ہیں۔ اور جب مدبر اور ام ولد اپنی ذات کے حق میں بیع کے تحت داخل نہیں ہوتے تو ان پر مشتری کا قبضہ بہت البیع بھی نہ ہوگا اور جب جہت البیع مقبوض نہ ہوئے بلکہ یوں ہی مالک کی اجازت سے مقبوض ہو گئے تو مر جانے کی صورت میں مشتری پر ان کا ضمان بھی واجب نہ ہوگا۔ کیونکہ ضمان مقبوض بہت البیع کی صورت میں واجب ہوتا ہے۔
The commentary of Ashraf al-Hidayah in Urdu, volume eight, is not but only so that the ruling of sale is established in the thing mixed with them. So it became as if the buyer's property does not enter alone into the ruling of his sale, rather the ruling of entry is established only in that property which the seller mixed with the buyer's property. The same ruling applies to mudabbar and umm walad. Explanation: The scenario is that if umm walad or mudabbar dies in the buyer's possession, then according to Imam Abu Hanifa no guarantee is obligatory on the buyer, and according to the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) guarantee with price is obligatory. This is one narration from Imam Abu Hanifa. The text of Hidayah indicates that for both mudabbar and umm walad there are two narrations from Imam: one of non-obligation of guarantee and one of obligation. However this is incorrect; rather the correct is that from Imam Abu Hanifa there are two narrations regarding mudabbar: if mudabbar dies in buyer's possession, one narration says no guarantee, the second says guarantee with price is obligatory. For umm walad, all narrations from Imam Abu Hanifa agree on non-obligation of guarantee, i.e., if umm walad dies in buyer's possession, only this narration exists that no guarantee is obligatory. The proof of the two companions is that the buyer's possession over mudabbar and umm walad is possession by virtue of sale, and it is possession by virtue of sale because both mudabbar and umm walad enter under the contract of sale. This is why if a slave is sold mixed with a mudabbar or umm walad, the buyer becomes owner of that slave in exchange for his share of the price. If mudabbar and umm walad did not enter under the contract of sale, the buyer would never own the slave sold mixed with them, just as if someone sells a free man and a slave together, the buyer does not own the slave because the free man with whom the slave is sold does not enter under the sale contract. In any case, it is established that mudabbar and umm walad enter under the sale contract, and whatever enters under the sale contract, the buyer's possession over it is possession by virtue of sale, and that which is possessed by virtue of sale is guaranteed, i.e., in case of destruction the possessor is liable for guarantee, just as other properties possessed on the basis of a sale are guaranteed. So if mudabbar or umm walad dies in the buyer's possession, guarantee is obligatory on the buyer. This is the answer to the objection regarding mukatab from the two companions. The objection is: if entering under the sale contract and establishing the buyer's ownership over the thing sold with it is the cause for guarantee, then the same should apply to mukatab: if mukatab dies in buyer's possession, guarantee should be obligatory on the buyer, because mukatab also enters under the sale contract and if a slave is sold mixed with him, the buyer becomes owner of that slave in exchange for his share of the price. Yet according to the two companions, if mukatab dies in the buyer's possession, guarantee is not obligatory. Why? The answer is that because the mukatab has possession over his own person, the buyer's possession is not actualized over him. Since guarantee is due because of possession, when buyer's possession over mukatab is not actualized, no guarantee is obligatory. The gist is that the basis of guarantee is the buyer's possession, not entering under the contract nor ownership of the thing sold mixed. So when the basis of guarantee (possession) is not found, guarantee is not obligatory. The proof of Imam Abu Hanifa is that the aspect of sale is a cause of guarantee only in those properties wherein the aspect of sale can be attached to the reality of sale, and the aspect of sale is attached to the reality of sale in properties that accept the reality of sale. Since mudabbar and umm walad do not accept the reality of sale like mukatab, the aspect of sale cannot be attached to the reality of sale for them, and therefore the aspect of sale does not cause guarantee. Since it does not cause guarantee, if mudabbar or umm walad die in buyer's possession, no guarantee is obligatory. The phrase 'and their entry into the sale' is a response to the companions' proof. The gist of the response is that mudabbar and umm walad are not subject to sale, so they do not enter under the contract of sale as far as their own persons are concerned; rather they enter only so that the ruling of sale (i.e., buyer's ownership) is established in the thing (e.g., slave) sold mixed with them. This is not far-fetched; there is a parallel in Shariah. For instance, if someone sells his own slave and Khalid's slave together to Khalid, then Khalid becomes owner of the seller's slave in exchange for his share of the price. Thus the contract of sale is valid regarding the seller's slave, and Khalid's slave, although not entering under the sale as far as his own person is concerned, enters under the sale to establish the ruling of sale (buyer's ownership) in the seller's slave. Similarly here, mudabbar and umm walad, although not entering under the sale as far as their own persons are concerned, enter under the sale to establish the buyer's ownership in the slave sold mixed with them. And when mudabbar and umm walad do not enter under the sale as far as their own persons are concerned, the buyer's possession over them is not possession by virtue of sale; rather they are possessed merely with the owner's permission. So if they die, no guarantee is obligatory on the buyer, because guarantee is obligatory only for possession by virtue of sale.
Source pages p. 164

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute concerning whether a mudabbar (a slave who will be freed upon the master's death) or umm walad (a slave woman who has borne a child to her master) causes guarantee (daman) if they die in the buyer's possession when sold mixed with another slave. The core of the dispute is whether these persons enter under the contract of sale for themselves or merely as a means to validate the sale of the accompanying slave. Imam Abu Hanifa holds that they do not enter the sale for themselves because they are not subject to sale (they are owned but cannot be sold outright due to their special status), so the buyer's possession over them is not 'possession by virtue of sale' (qabd bi-ḥukm al-bayʿ) and thus no guarantee is due upon their death. The two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) argue that since the buyer becomes owner of the accompanying slave because of their inclusion, they must have entered the sale contract, making the buyer's possession a sale-based possession, thus guarantee is obligatory. The text clarifies that for mudabbar there are two narrations from Abu Hanifa (non-obligation and obligation), but for umm walad all narrations agree on non-obligation. The companions' objection regarding mukatab is answered by noting that the mukatab himself has possession over his own person, so the buyer's possession is not actualized. The commentator then provides Abu Hanifa's own proof: the 'aspect of sale' (jihat al-bayʿ) causes guarantee only in properties that can genuinely be sold; mudabbar and umm walad cannot be genuinely sold (like free persons or mukatab), so the aspect of sale cannot attach to them. The final resolution: they enter the sale only to facilitate ownership of the mixed property, not for themselves, so no guarantee. This passage exemplifies Hanafi istiḥsān (juristic preference) and careful distinction between legal capacity and actual subject matter.

Key Terms
مدبر (mudabbar): A slave who is promised freedom upon the master's death, making him unsellable in a normal sale but allowing sale only when mixed with another property to facilitate transfer.
ام ولد (umm walad): A slave woman who has borne a child to her master, gaining freedom upon master's death; similar to mudabbar in sale restrictions.
ضمان (ḍamān): Financial liability/guarantee; here it means the buyer must pay the price if the sold item perishes in his possession (if possession is bi-ḥukm al-bayʿ).
قبضہ بہت البیع (qabḍ bi-ḥukm al-bayʿ): Possession taken under the contract of sale, which creates guarantee.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the mufta bihi in the Hanafi school, what is the ruling when a mudabbar dies in the buyer's possession after being sold mixed with another slave?
A) No guarantee is obligatory on the buyer.
B) Guarantee is obligatory on the buyer, and he must pay the price.
C) Guarantee is obligatory only if the buyer knew the status of the mudabbar.
D) The sale is void, and the property reverts to the seller.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, the mufta bihi is that mudabbar and umm walad sold mixed create guarantee upon death in buyer's possession, due to their entry into the sale contract.

Buyu — Sales and Trade
advanced
12 min
The Legal Proof: Entry and Possession in Mixed Sales
Intra-Hanafi dispute on daman

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the analogy (qiyas) used by both sides in the mudabbar/umm walad guarantee dispute and evaluate the strength of Abu Hanifa's response.

Core Idea
Entry into a sale contract can be for the sake of another; possession by virtue of sale requires entry for oneself.

This lesson unpacks the legal reasoning behind the intra-Hanafi dispute on guarantee for mudabbar and umm walad. Both sides use qiyas. The Sahibayn analogize to ordinary property; Abu Hanifa distinguishes between entering for oneself and entering to facilitate sale of another. We also examine the critical objection regarding mukatab and its resolution.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Sahibayn's qiyas
The Sahibayn argue: Any property that enters the sale contract is possessed bi-ḥukm al-bayʿ and thus guaranteed. Mudabbar and umm walad enter the contract because the buyer becomes owner of the mixed slave only by including them. Therefore, guarantee.
2
Identify Abu Hanifa's counter-qiyas
Abu Hanifa analogizes to a free man: a free man sold mixed does not enter the sale, so the buyer does not own the accompanying slave. Similarly, mudabbar/umm walad do not accept the reality of sale, so they do not enter for themselves.
3
Analyze the illa (effective cause)
Abu Hanifa's illa is that the aspect of sale (jihat al-bayʿ) only attaches to properties that genuinely accept sale (haqiqat al-bayʿ). Mudabbar and umm walad, like mukatab, do not accept true sale, so jihat al-bayʿ does not attach.
4
Resolve the mukatab objection
The mukatab also enters the sale contract, yet no guarantee because the buyer's possession is not actualized (mukatab possesses himself). This proves that possession, not entry, is the basis of guarantee.
5
Identify the parallel (tathir)
The example of Khalid's slave sold with the seller's slave: Khalid's slave enters the contract to validate the seller's slave's sale, but Khalid's slave is not bought. Similarly, mudabbar/umm walad enter only to validate the mixed property's sale, not for themselves.

عدم وجوب ضمان پر متفق ہیں یعنی اگر مشتری کے قبضہ میں ام ولد مرگئی تو امام صاحب سے صرف یہ روایت ہے کہ مشتری پر ضمان واجب نہ ہوگا۔ صاحبین کی دلیل یہ ہےکہ مدبر اورام ولد پر مشتری کا قبضہ بہت البیع ہوتا ہے اور بہت البیع قبضہ اسلئے ہوتا ہے کہ مد بر اورام ولد دونوں عقد بیع کے تحت داخل ہو جاتے ہیں۔ یہی وجہ ہے کہ مدبر اور ام ولد کے ساتھ اگر کوئی غلام ملا کر فروخت کیا گیا تو مشتری اس غلام کا اس کے حصہ ثمن کے عوض مالک ہو جاتا ہے۔ اگر مد بر اورام ولد عقد بیع کے تحت داخل نہ ہوتے تو جو غلام ان کے ساتھ ملا کر فروخت کیا گیا ہے۔ مشتری اس کا مالک ہرگز نہ ہوتا جیسے اگر کوئی آزاد آدمی اور غلام کو ملا کر فروخت کر دے تو مشتری غلام کا مالک نہیں ہوتا۔ کیونکہ آزاد آدمی جس کے ساتھ ملا کر غلام فروخت کیا گیا ہے وہ عقد بیع کے تحت داخل نہیں ہوتا۔ بہر حال یہ بات ثابت ہوگئی کہ مد بر اورام ولد عقد بیع کے تحت داخل ہوتے ہیں اور جو چیز عقد بیع کے تحت داخل ہوتی ہے۔ اس پر مشتری کا قبضہ بہت البیع ہوتا ہے اور مقبوض بہت البيع مضمون ہوتا ہے یعنی ہلاکت کی صورت میں قابض پر ضمان واجب ہوتا ہے۔ جیسا کہ دوسرے اموال ، مقبوض علی سوم الشراء کی صورت میں مضمون ہوتے ہیں۔ اگر مد بریا ام ولد مشتری کے قبضہ میں مرجائے تو مشتری پر اس کا ضمان واجب ہو گا۔ بخلاف المکاتب سے صاحبین کی طرف سے سوال کا جواب ہے۔ سوال یہ ہے کہ اگر کسی چیز کا عقد بیع کے تحت داخل ہونا اور جو چیز اس کے ساتھ ملا کر فروخت کی گئی ہے۔ اس پر مشتری کی ملکیت کا ثابت ہونا ضمان واجب ہونے کا سبب ہے تو مکاتب کے حق میں بھی یہ بات ہونی چاہئے تھی کہ مکاتب اگر مشتری کے قبضہ میں مرجائے تو مشتری پر اس کا ضمان واجب ہو، کیونکہ مکاتب عقد بیع کے تحت بھی داخل ہوتا ہے اور اگر غلام اس کے ساتھ ملا کر بیچا جائے تو مشتری اس غلام کا اس کے حصہ ثمن کے عوض مالک بھی ہو جاتا ہے۔ حالانکہ مکاتب اگر مشتری کے قبضہ میں مر جائے تو صاحبین کے نزدیک مشتری پر مکاتب کا ضمان واجب نہیں ہوتا۔ ایسا کیوں ہے؟ اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ مکاتب کا قبضہ ہی اپنی ذات پر چونکہ خود ہوتا ہے۔ اسلئے اس کے حق میں مشتری کا قبضہ متحقق نہ ہوگا ۔ حالانکہ یہ ضمان قبضہ ہی کی وجہ سے واجب ہوتا ہے۔ پس جب مکاتب پر مشتری کا قبضہ ہی متحقق نہ ہوا تو مشتری پر اس کا ضمان بھی واجب نہ ہوگا۔ حاصل یہ کہ وجوب ضمان کا مدار مشتری کا قبضہ ہے نہ عقد کے تحت داخل ہونا ہے اور نہ اس چیز کا مالک ہوتا ہے جس کو اسکے ساتھ ملا کر فروخت کیا ہے۔ پس جب مدار ضمان یعنی قبضہ نہیں پایا گیا تو مشتری پر مکاتب کا ضمان بھی واجب نہ ہوگا۔ حضرت امام ابو حنیفہ کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ جہت بیع ان اموال میں موجب ضمان ہے جن اموال میں جہت بیع کو حقیقت بیع کے ساتھ لاحق کیا جا سکتا ہو اور جہت بیع کو حقیقت بیع کے ساتھ ان اموال میں لاحق کیا جاتا ہے جو اموال حقیقت بیع کو قبول کرتے ہوں۔ اور مدبر اور ام ولد چونکہ مکاتب کی طرح حقیقت بیع کو قبول نہیں کرتے اسلئے ان کے حق میں جہت بیع کو حقیقت بیع کے ساتھ لاحق نہیں کیا جا سکتا ہے اور جب ان کے حق میں جہت بیع کو حقیقت بیع کے ساتھ لاحق نہیں کیا جا سکتا تو جہت بیع موجب ضمان بھی نہ ہوگی۔ اور جب جہت بیع موجب ضمان نہیں تو مدبر اور ام ولد اگر مشتری کے قبضہ میں مرجائیں تو مشتری پر ان کا ضمان واجب نہ ہوگا۔ وليس دخولهما في البيع سے صاحبین کی دلیل کا جواب ہے۔ جواب کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ مد بر اور ام ولد چونکہ بیع کا محل نہیں ہیں۔ اسلئے یہ دونوں خود اپنی ذات کے حق میں عقد بیع کے تحت داخل نہیں ہوتے ہیں بلکہ صرف اسلئے بیع کے تحت داخل ہوتے ہیں تا کہ جو چیز یعنی غلام وغیرہ ان کے ساتھ ملا کر فروخت کی گئی ہے اس میں بیع کا حکم یعنی مشتری کی ملکیت ثابت ہو جائے اور ایسا ہونا مستبعد نہیں ہے بلکہ شریعت میں اس کی نظیر موجود ہے۔ چنانچہ اگر کسی نے اپنا غلام اور خالد کا غلام ملا کر خالد کے ہاتھ فروخت کر دیا تو خالد بائع کے غلام کا اس کے حصہ ثمن کے عوض مالک ہو جاتا ہے۔ پس بائع کے غلام کے حق میں عقد بیع درست ہو گیا اور مشتری یعنی خالد کا غلام عقد بیع کے تحت خود اپنی ذات کے حق میں اگر چہ داخل نہیں ہوا لیکن بائع کے غلام میں حکم بیع یعنی مشتری کی ملک ثابت کرنے کیلئے بیع کے تحت داخل ہو گیا ہے۔ اسی طرح یہاں مدبر اور ام ولد اگر چہ خود اپنی ذات کے حق میں عقد بیع کے تحت داخل نہیں ہوئے لیکن جو غلام ان کے ساتھ ملا کر بیچا گیا ہے اس کے اندر مشتری کی ملک ثابت کرنے کیلئے عقد بیع کے تحت داخل ہو گئے ہیں۔ اور جب مدبر اور ام ولد اپنی ذات کے حق میں بیع کے تحت داخل نہیں ہوتے تو ان پر مشتری کا قبضہ بہت البیع بھی نہ ہوگا اور جب جہت البیع مقبوض نہ ہوئے بلکہ یوں ہی مالک کی اجازت سے مقبوض ہو گئے تو مر جانے کی صورت میں مشتری پر ان کا ضمان بھی واجب نہ ہوگا۔ کیونکہ ضمان مقبوض بہت البیع کی صورت میں واجب ہوتا ہے۔
The commentary of Ashraf al-Hidayah in Urdu, volume eight, is not but only so that the ruling of sale is established in the thing mixed with them. So it became as if the buyer's property does not enter alone into the ruling of his sale, rather the ruling of entry is established only in that property which the seller mixed with the buyer's property. The same ruling applies to mudabbar and umm walad. Explanation: The scenario is that if umm walad or mudabbar dies in the buyer's possession, then according to Imam Abu Hanifa no guarantee is obligatory on the buyer, and according to the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) guarantee with price is obligatory. This is one narration from Imam Abu Hanifa. The text of Hidayah indicates that for both mudabbar and umm walad there are two narrations from Imam: one of non-obligation of guarantee and one of obligation. However this is incorrect; rather the correct is that from Imam Abu Hanifa there are two narrations regarding mudabbar: if mudabbar dies in buyer's possession, one narration says no guarantee, the second says guarantee with price is obligatory. For umm walad, all narrations from Imam Abu Hanifa agree on non-obligation of guarantee, i.e., if umm walad dies in buyer's possession, only this narration exists that no guarantee is obligatory. The proof of the two companions is that the buyer's possession over mudabbar and umm walad is possession by virtue of sale, and it is possession by virtue of sale because both mudabbar and umm walad enter under the contract of sale. This is why if a slave is sold mixed with a mudabbar or umm walad, the buyer becomes owner of that slave in exchange for his share of the price. If mudabbar and umm walad did not enter under the contract of sale, the buyer would never own the slave sold mixed with them, just as if someone sells a free man and a slave together, the buyer does not own the slave because the free man with whom the slave is sold does not enter under the sale contract. In any case, it is established that mudabbar and umm walad enter under the sale contract, and whatever enters under the sale contract, the buyer's possession over it is possession by virtue of sale, and that which is possessed by virtue of sale is guaranteed, i.e., in case of destruction the possessor is liable for guarantee, just as other properties possessed on the basis of a sale are guaranteed. So if mudabbar or umm walad dies in the buyer's possession, guarantee is obligatory on the buyer. This is the answer to the objection regarding mukatab from the two companions. The objection is: if entering under the sale contract and establishing the buyer's ownership over the thing sold with it is the cause for guarantee, then the same should apply to mukatab: if mukatab dies in buyer's possession, guarantee should be obligatory on the buyer, because mukatab also enters under the sale contract and if a slave is sold mixed with him, the buyer becomes owner of that slave in exchange for his share of the price. Yet according to the two companions, if mukatab dies in the buyer's possession, guarantee is not obligatory. Why? The answer is that because the mukatab has possession over his own person, the buyer's possession is not actualized over him. Since guarantee is due because of possession, when buyer's possession over mukatab is not actualized, no guarantee is obligatory. The gist is that the basis of guarantee is the buyer's possession, not entering under the contract nor ownership of the thing sold mixed. So when the basis of guarantee (possession) is not found, guarantee is not obligatory. The proof of Imam Abu Hanifa is that the aspect of sale is a cause of guarantee only in those properties wherein the aspect of sale can be attached to the reality of sale, and the aspect of sale is attached to the reality of sale in properties that accept the reality of sale. Since mudabbar and umm walad do not accept the reality of sale like mukatab, the aspect of sale cannot be attached to the reality of sale for them, and therefore the aspect of sale does not cause guarantee. Since it does not cause guarantee, if mudabbar or umm walad die in buyer's possession, no guarantee is obligatory. The phrase 'and their entry into the sale' is a response to the companions' proof. The gist of the response is that mudabbar and umm walad are not subject to sale, so they do not enter under the contract of sale as far as their own persons are concerned; rather they enter only so that the ruling of sale (i.e., buyer's ownership) is established in the thing (e.g., slave) sold mixed with them. This is not far-fetched; there is a parallel in Shariah. For instance, if someone sells his own slave and Khalid's slave together to Khalid, then Khalid becomes owner of the seller's slave in exchange for his share of the price. Thus the contract of sale is valid regarding the seller's slave, and Khalid's slave, although not entering under the sale as far as his own person is concerned, enters under the sale to establish the ruling of sale (buyer's ownership) in the seller's slave. Similarly here, mudabbar and umm walad, although not entering under the sale as far as their own persons are concerned, enter under the sale to establish the buyer's ownership in the slave sold mixed with them. And when mudabbar and umm walad do not enter under the sale as far as their own persons are concerned, the buyer's possession over them is not possession by virtue of sale; rather they are possessed merely with the owner's permission. So if they die, no guarantee is obligatory on the buyer, because guarantee is obligatory only for possession by virtue of sale.
Source pages p. 164

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute concerning whether a mudabbar (a slave who will be freed upon the master's death) or umm walad (a slave woman who has borne a child to her master) causes guarantee (daman) if they die in the buyer's possession when sold mixed with another slave. The core of the dispute is whether these persons enter under the contract of sale for themselves or merely as a means to validate the sale of the accompanying slave. Imam Abu Hanifa holds that they do not enter the sale for themselves because they are not subject to sale (they are owned but cannot be sold outright due to their special status), so the buyer's possession over them is not 'possession by virtue of sale' (qabd bi-ḥukm al-bayʿ) and thus no guarantee is due upon their death. The two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) argue that since the buyer becomes owner of the accompanying slave because of their inclusion, they must have entered the sale contract, making the buyer's possession a sale-based possession, thus guarantee is obligatory. The text clarifies that for mudabbar there are two narrations from Abu Hanifa (non-obligation and obligation), but for umm walad all narrations agree on non-obligation. The companions' objection regarding mukatab is answered by noting that the mukatab himself has possession over his own person, so the buyer's possession is not actualized. The commentator then provides Abu Hanifa's own proof: the 'aspect of sale' (jihat al-bayʿ) causes guarantee only in properties that can genuinely be sold; mudabbar and umm walad cannot be genuinely sold (like free persons or mukatab), so the aspect of sale cannot attach to them. The final resolution: they enter the sale only to facilitate ownership of the mixed property, not for themselves, so no guarantee. This passage exemplifies Hanafi istiḥsān (juristic preference) and careful distinction between legal capacity and actual subject matter.

Key Terms
مدبر (mudabbar): A slave promised freedom upon master's death.
ام ولد (umm walad): Slave woman who bore child to master.
جہت البیع (jihat al-bayʿ): The aspect or legal dimension of sale that makes possession by virtue of sale.
حقیقت البیع (haqiqat al-bayʿ): The reality of sale as a contract transferring ownership for a price.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the basis (madar) of guarantee according to both Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn after resolving the mukatab objection?
A) Entry into the contract of sale
B) Ownership of the mixed property
C) Actual possession (qabḍ) by the buyer
D) The seller's intention to transfer ownership

Key Takeaway
Guarantee (daman) arises from actual possession (qabḍ) by virtue of sale, not merely from entering the sale contract.

Buyu — Sales and Trade
beginner
6 min
Ruling on Selling Fish Before Catching and in Enclosure
Ruling statement on prohibition of selling fish before capture and in an enclosure lacking deliverability

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on selling fish before capture and identify the conditions that make sale in an enclosure valid or invalid.

Core Idea
You cannot sell what you do not own or cannot deliver.

This passage from al-Quduri's Mukhtasar establishes a key principle in Hanafi sales law: the seller must own the item and be able to deliver it at the time of contract. The specific case of fish illustrates this: selling fish before catching them is invalid because neither ownership nor deliverability exists. Similarly, selling fish in an enclosure (khaẓīrah) is conditional on whether the fish can be taken easily (without hunting) and whether the seller has actually possessed them. Understanding this ruling helps you apply the broader requirement of ability to deliver (maqdūr al-taslīm) in various transactions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two main scenarios
The passage covers two cases: selling fish before they are caught, and selling fish that are already in an enclosure. Distinguish between them.
2
State the ruling for each scenario
Selling fish before catching is invalid (bāṭil). Selling fish in an enclosure is invalid unless the fish can be taken without difficulty and the seller has actually possessed them.
The ruling is bāṭil because the condition of ownership and ability to deliver is missing.
3
Identify the key legal condition
The condition is 'ability to deliver' (maqdūr al-taslīm). If the fish cannot be handed over easily, the sale is invalid.
Also ownership (milk) is required; fish not caught are not owned.
4
Apply the condition to the enclosure case
If the fish are in an enclosure and require hunting (difficulty) to catch, sale is invalid. If they can be taken without a trick (easily), sale is valid—provided the seller has placed them there after catching them.
If fish gather by themselves and the entrance is not closed, the seller does not own them, so sale is invalid.
5
Note the exception
The exception is when fish are easily catchable from the enclosure, e.g., they are few or the water is shallow. Then sale is valid.
The determining factor is ease of capture, not merely the existence of an enclosure.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مچھلی کی شکار سے پہلے بیچ کا حکم
قال ولا يجوز بيع السمك قبل ان يصطاد لانه باع ما لا يملكه ولا في حظيرة اذا كان لا يؤخذ الابصيد لانه غير مقدور التسليم ومعناه اذا اخذه ثم القاه فيها ولو كان يؤخذ من غير حيلة جاز الا اذا اجتمعت فيها بانفسها ولم يسد عليها المدخل لعدم الملك
ترجمہ قدوری نے کہا اور شکار کرنے سے پہلے مچھلی کی بیع جائز نہیں ہے کیونکہ اس نے ایسی چیز فروخت کی جس کا وہ مالک نہیں ہے۔ اور خطیرہ (باڑہ) میں جائز نہیں جبکہ نہ پکڑی جائے مگر شکار کے ساتھ ۔ کیونکہ سپرد کرنا اس کی قدرت میں نہیں ہے اور اس کے معنی یہ ہیں کہ جب مشتری نے اس کو پکڑ کر خطیرہ میں ڈال دیا ہو اور اگر بغیر حیلہ کے پکڑی جاسکتی ہو تو جائز ہے مگر جبکہ خطیرہ میں مچھلیاں خود بیج ہو گئیں اور داخل ہونے کا راستہ بند نہیں کیا ( تو بیع جائز نہیں ہے ) کیونکہ ملک معدوم ہے۔
تشریح خطیرہ باڑہ یعنی وہ جگہ جس کو جانوروں کے رہنے کیلئے گھیر دیا ہو اور لکڑیوں کی باڑ کر دی ہو ۔ اس جگہ خطیرہ سے مراد پانی کا گڑھا ہے کیونکہ مچھلیوں کے نکلنے سے وہ بھی رکاوٹ بنتا ہے۔ اسلئے اس کو خطیرہ کہا گیا ہے۔ اصولی طور پر یہ بات ذہن میں رہے کہ
Ruling on selling fish before catching. He (al-Quduri) said: The sale of fish before it is caught is not permissible because he sold what he does not own. Nor is it permissible in a haẓīrah (enclosure) when it cannot be taken except by hunting, because it is not capable of delivery. Its meaning is when he has taken it and then thrown it into it (the enclosure). If it can be taken without a trick (without hunting), it is permissible, except when they (fish) gather in it by themselves and he has not closed the entrance (then sale is not permissible) due to lack of ownership. Translation: Al-Quduri said: And selling fish before hunting is not permissible because he sold something he does not own. And in a khaẓīrah (enclosure) it is not permissible when it is not caught except by hunting, because he is not able to deliver. Its meaning is when he has taken it and then thrown it into it. If it can be taken without a trick, it is permissible, except when fish gather in it by themselves and the entrance is not closed (then sale is not permissible) because ownership is non-existent. Explanation: Khaẓīrah (enclosure) is a place that is fenced with wood for animals. Here it means a pit of water because it also acts as a barrier to prevent fish from escaping, hence it is called khaẓīrah. Bear in mind as a principle that...
Source pages p. 165

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement from al-Quduri's Mukhtasar, cited and explained by the commentator. It addresses two scenarios: (1) selling fish before catching them, which is invalid because the fish are not owned and not deliverable (ghayr maqdūr al-taslīm). (2) Selling fish that are in an enclosure (haẓīrah/khaẓīrah) such that they cannot be caught without difficulty (hunting). If the fish are in an enclosure but can be caught easily (without a trick, i.e., by hand or net easily), the sale is valid. However, if they gathered in the enclosure by themselves (without being put there), and the entrance is not closed, then the sale is invalid because the fish are not owned (they are still like wild fish). The principle: ownership of fish is established only by actual possession (qabd). The commentator adds a brief explanation of khaẓīrah as a fenced area or water pit. This lesson is part of the section on what cannot be sold due to lack of ownership or deliverability.

Key Terms
خطیرہ (khaẓīrah): An enclosure, specifically a water pit or fenced area where fish are kept; sale validity depends on whether fish can be taken easily.
غیر مقدور التسلیم (ghayr maqdūr al-taslīm): Unable to deliver; a condition that renders the sale invalid because the seller cannot physically hand over the item.
شکار (shikār): Hunting; fish that require effort (like using a net) to catch are considered hunted.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A fisherman places a net enclosure in a river, fish enter by themselves, and he closes the entrance. He then sells the fish inside the enclosure without catching them. Is this sale valid according to the Hanafi school?
A) Yes, because the fish are now in his enclosure
B) No, because the fish are not yet caught and possessed
C) Yes, because the enclosure acts as possession
D) No, because fish can never be sold before catching

Key Takeaway
Sale of fish before catching is invalid due to lack of ownership and deliverability; for fish in an enclosure, validity depends on actual capture and ease of delivery.

Buyu — Sales and Trade
intermediate

Imam Abu Hanifa's Proof: No Liability for Mudabbar and Umm Walad in Sale
Imam Abu Hanifa's rational proof (dalil aqli) in an intra-Hanafi dispute.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why Imam Abu Hanifa holds that a mudabbar and umm walad sold with another slave do not incur liability and apply the concept of jiha al-bay' to similar cases.

Core Idea
The cause of sale creates liability only when attached to property that accepts the reality of sale.

This lesson delves into an intra-Hanafi dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and his two foremost students, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani. The crux is whether the buyer becomes liable for the value of a mudabbar or umm walad if they die in his possession after being sold together with another slave. Imam Abu Hanifa argues no, and his reasoning hinges on the legal concept of 'jiha al-bay'' (the cause of sale). Understanding this argument illuminates how Hanafi jurists analyze the foundations of liability in sales.

Guided Path
1
Identify the dispute and parties
Recognize that the disagreement is between Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) on whether a mudabbar or umm walad sold with another slave creates liability for the buyer if they perish.
The Sahibayn argue they are included in the sale; Abu Hanifa says their inclusion is only for perfecting the main sale.
2
Understand 'jiha al-bay''
Grasp the Hanafi technical term 'jiha al-bay'' (cause of sale) which is the legal basis for liability. It attaches either to the reality of taking (haqiqat al-akhdh) or the reality of sale (haqiqat al-bay'). Liability arises only when the cause attaches to property that can be validly sold.
Properties that cannot be sold (like mudabbar, umm walad, mukatab) do not accept the reality of sale.
3
Apply the concept to mudabbar and umm walad
Since mudabbar and umm walad cannot be validly sold (their sale is inherently invalid), the cause of sale cannot attach to them via the reality of sale. Hence, no liability arises from their inclusion in a sale contract.
Their inclusion in the contract is only to facilitate ownership transfer of the main slave.
4
Analyze the Sahibayn's objection
The Sahibayn cite the phrase 'wa laysa dukhulu huma fi al-bay'' (they are included in the sale) to argue that the mudabbar and umm walad are part of the sale, implying liability.
Imam Abu Hanifa counters that inclusion is not in their own right but for the sake of the main slave.
5
Evaluate the analogy with Khalid's slave
Imam Abu Hanifa gives an analogy: selling one's own slave together with Khalid's slave to Khalid. In that case, Khalid's slave enters the contract not as a subject of sale but to establish the buyer's ownership of the seller's slave. Similarly, mudabbar and umm walad enter the contract only to perfect the sale of the accompanying slave.
This shows that inclusion does not automatically create liability; the nature of the item matters.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
حضرت امام ابو حنیفہ کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ جہت بیع ان اموال میں موجب ضمان ہے جن اموال میں جہت بیع کو حقیقت لینا کے ساتھ لاحق کیا جا سکتا ہو اور جہت بیع کو حقیقت بیع کے ساتھ ان اموال میں لاحق کیا جاتا ہے جو اموال حقیقت بیع کو قبول کرتے ہوں۔ اور مدبر اور ام ولد چونکہ مکاتب کی طرح حقیقت بیع کو قبول نہیں کرتے اسلئے ان کے حق میں جہت بیع کو حقیقت بیع کے ساتھ لاحق نہیں کیا جا سکتا ہے اور جب ان کے حق میں جہت بیع کو حقیقت بیع کے ساتھ لاحق نہیں کیا جا سکتا تو جہت بیع موجب ضمان بھی نہ ہوگی۔ اور جب جہت بیع موجب ضمان نہیں تو مدبر اور ام ولد اگر مشتری کے قبضہ میں مرجائیں تو مشتری پر ان کا ضمان واجب نہ ہوگا۔ وليس دخولهما في البيع سے صاحبین کی دلیل کا جواب ہے۔ جواب کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ مدبر اور ام ولد چونکہ بیع کا محل نہیں ہیں۔ اسلئے یہ دونوں خود اپنی ذات کے حق میں عقد بیع کے تحت داخل نہیں ہوتے ہیں بلکہ صرف اسلئے بیع کے تحت داخل ہوتے ہیں تا کہ جو چیز یعنی غلام وغیرہ ان کے ساتھ ملا کر فروخت کی گئی ہے اس میں بیع کا حکم یعنی مشتری کی ملکیت ثابت ہو جائے اور ایسا ہونا مستبعد نہیں ہے بلکہ شریعت میں اس کی نظیر موجود ہے۔ چنانچہ اگر کسی نے اپنا غلام اور خالد کا غلام ملا کر خالہ کے ہاتھ فروخت کر دیا تو خالد بائع کے غلام کا اس کے حصہ ثمن کے عوض مالک ہو جاتا ہے۔ پس بائع کے غلام کے حق میں عقد بیع درست ہو گیا اور مشتری یعنی خالد کا غلام عقد بیع کے تحت خود اپنی ذات کے حق میں اگر چہ داخل نہیں ہوا لیکن بائع کے غلام میں حکم بیع یعنی مشتری کی ملک ثابت کرنے کیلئے بیع کے تحت داخل ہو گیا ہے۔ اسی طرح یہاں مدبر اور ام ولد اگر چہ خود اپنی ذات کے حق میں عقد بیع کے تحت داخل نہیں ہوئے لیکن جو غلام ان کے ساتھ ملا کر بیچا گیا ہے اس کے اندر مشتری کی ملک ثابت کرنے کیلئے عقد بیع کے تحت داخل ہو گئے ہیں۔ اور جب مدبر اور ام ولد اپنی ذات کے حق میں بیع کے تحت داخل نہیں ہوتے تو ان پر مشتری کا قبضہ بہت البیع بھی نہ ہوگا اور جب جہت البیع مقبوض نہ ہوئے بلکہ یوں ہی مالک کی اجازت سے مقبوض ہو گئے تو مر جانے کی صورت میں مشتری پر ان کا ضمان بھی واجب نہ ہوگا۔ کیونکہ ضمان مقبوض بعت البیع کی صورت میں واجب ہوتا ہے۔
The proof of Hadrat Imam Abu Hanifa is that the cause of sale is a source of liability in those properties in which the cause of sale can be attached to the reality of taking, and the cause of sale is attached to the reality of sale in those properties that accept the reality of sale. And since a mudabbar and an umm walad, like a mukatab, do not accept the reality of sale, therefore in their regard the cause of sale cannot be attached to the reality of sale. And when the cause of sale cannot be attached to the reality of sale in their regard, then the cause of sale will not be a source of liability. And when the cause of sale is not a source of liability, then if a mudabbar and an umm walad die in the buyer's possession, their liability will not be obligatory upon the buyer. And 'و ليس دخولهما في البيع' is the answer to the proof of the Sahibayn. The summary of the answer is that since a mudabbar and an umm walad are not the subject of sale, therefore they themselves do not enter under the contract of sale in their own right; rather, they only enter under the sale so that the ruling of sale, i.e., the buyer's ownership, may be established in the item that was sold mixed with them, such as a slave, etc. And this is not unlikely; rather, there is an analogy in the Shari'ah. For example, if someone sold his own slave and Khalid's slave together to Khalid, then Khalid becomes the owner of the seller's slave in exchange for his share of the price. So the contract of sale became valid with respect to the seller's slave, and the buyer, i.e., Khalid's slave, even though he did not enter under the contract of sale in his own right, yet entered under the sale for the purpose of establishing the ruling of sale, i.e., the buyer's ownership, in the seller's slave. Similarly here, the mudabbar and the umm walad, even though they did not enter under the contract of sale in their own right, yet they entered under the contract of sale for the purpose of establishing the buyer's ownership in the slave sold mixed with them. And when the mudabbar and the umm walad do not enter under the sale in their own right, then the buyer's possession over them will not be by virtue of the sale; and when their being possessed [by the buyer] is not by virtue of the sale but rather they are possessed simply with the owner's permission, then in the case of their death, their liability will not be obligatory upon the buyer, because liability is obligatory in the case of possession by virtue of sale.
Source pages p. 165

Commentary
This passage presents Imam Abu Hanifa's argument in an intra-Hanafi dispute with the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) regarding the liability of a mudabbar and an umm walad when sold together with another slave. The issue is whether the buyer becomes liable for their value if they die in his possession. Abu Hanifa argues that the cause of sale (jiha al-bay') only creates liability when it attaches to property that can be the subject of a valid sale. Since a mudabbar and umm walad cannot be validly sold (like a mukatab), the cause of sale does not attach to them in reality, and thus no liability arises. The Sahibayn had argued that they are included in the sale (dakhil fi al-bay') based on the text 'wa laysa dukhulu huma fi al-bay''. Abu Hanifa's response is that their inclusion is only for the purpose of perfecting the sale of the main slave, not for their own sake. He illustrates with an analogy: if a man sells his own slave together with Khalid's slave to Khalid, the contract is valid for the seller's slave, and Khalid's slave enters the sale not in his own right but to establish ownership in the seller's slave. Similarly, the mudabbar and umm walad are included only to establish the buyer's ownership in the accompanying slave. Since their possession by the buyer is not by virtue of the sale (but rather by the owner's permission), no liability for their death arises.

Key Terms
جہت بیع (jiha al-bay'): The aspect of sale that creates liability; it attaches to property that accepts the reality of sale.
ضمان (daman): Liability for the value of goods; here, the buyer's obligation to compensate if the sold item perishes in his possession.
مدبر (mudabbar): A slave promised freedom upon the master's death; cannot be sold in a valid sale.
ام ولد (umm walad): A slave woman who has borne a child to her master; she becomes free upon his death and cannot be sold.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Because the mudabbar does not accept the reality of sale, so the cause of sale does not attach.
C) Because the buyer did not physically take possession.
D) Because the mudabbar becomes free upon the seller's death.

Key Takeaway
The cause of sale only creates liability when attached to property that accepts the reality of sale; mudabbar and umm walad do not.

Buyu — Sales and Trade
