Conditions for Validity of Selling Fish: Ownership and Ability to Deliver
Ruling on selling fish before catching and in a pond

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions for a valid sale of fish in Hanafi fiqh and apply them to different scenarios involving ponds and delivery capability.

Core Idea
A sale requires both ownership and ability to deliver; selling uncaptured fish fails both.

Selling fish before catching them seems straightforward, but Islamic law imposes two critical conditions: the seller must own the item and be able to deliver it physically. This lesson examines the Hanafi ruling on selling fish in open water versus enclosed ponds, clarifying when a sale is valid or invalid. The classic text from al-Quduri and its commentary guide us through the nuances.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is selling fish before catching or in a pond. The ruling is not permissible (la yajuz) unless specific conditions are met.
The default ruling is invalidity.
2
Extract the two essential conditions
From the text, deduce that for a sale to be valid, the item must be owned by the seller (mamluk) and within his ability to deliver (maqdur al-taslim).
These are general sale conditions in Hanafi fiqh.
3
Apply to fish scenarios
Apply the conditions to river fish (not owned) and pond fish (owned but possibly not deliverable). The text distinguishes between small and large ponds, and whether fish gathered naturally or were placed.
Focus on the 'khalirah' (enclosed pond) cases.
4
Note the khiyar al-ru'yah
Even when the sale is valid, the buyer retains the option of seeing (khiyar al-ru'yah) because underwater sight differs from dry sight.
This is an additional consumer protection.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مچھلی کی شکار سے پہلے بیع کا حکم
قال ولا يجوز بيع السمك قبل ان يصطاد لانه باع ما لا يملكه ولا في حظيرة اذا كان لا يؤخذ الابصيد لانه غير مقدور التسليم ومعناه اذا اخذه ثم القاه فيها ولو كان يؤخذ من غير حيلة جاز الا اذا اجتمعت فيها بانفسها ولم يسد عليها المدخل لعدم الملك
ترجمہ قدوری نے کہا اور شکار کرنے سے پہلے مچھلی کی بیع جائز نہیں ہے کیونکہ اس نے ایسی چیز فروخت کی جس کا وہ مالک نہیں ہے۔ اور خطیرہ (باڑہ) میں جائز نہیں جبکہ نہ پکڑی جائے مگر شکار کے ساتھ ۔ کیونکہ سپرد کرنا اس کی قدرت میں نہیں ہے اور اس کے معنی یہ ہیں کہ جب مشتری نے اس کو پکڑ کر خطیرہ میں ڈالدیا ہو اور اگر بغیر حیلہ کے پکڑی جاسکتی ہو تو جائز ہے مگر جبکہ خطیرہ میں مچھلیاں خود بیج ہو گئیں اور داخل ہونے کا راستہ بند نہیں کیا ( تو بیع جائز نہیں ہے ) کیونکہ ملک معدوم ہے۔ تشریح خطیرہ باڑہ یعنی وہ جگہ جس کو جانوروں کے رہنے کیلئے گھیر دیا ہو اور لکڑیوں کی باڑ کر دی ہو ۔ اس جگہ خطیرہ سے مراد پانی کا گڑھا ہے کیونکہ مچھلیوں کے نکلنے سے وہ بھی رکاوٹ بنتا ہے۔ اسلئے اس کو خطیرہ کہا گیا ہے۔ اصولی طور پر یہ بات ذہن میں رہے کہ
جواز بیع کیلئے مبیع کا بائع کی ملک اور مقدور التسلیم ہونا ضروری ہے اگر مبیع بائع کی ملوک نہ ہو یا مملو تو ہومگر مقدور التسلیم نہ ہو تو بیع جائز نہ ہوگی۔ صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ شکار کرنے سے پہلے دریا یا نہر وغیرہ میں مچھلی کا فروخت کرنا جائز نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ مچھلی جب تنگ در پایا تالاب میں ہو تب تک وہ کسی کی ملک نہیں ہوتی بلکہ مباح ہوتی ہے ہر شخص اس کو پکڑ سکتا ہے اور غیر مملوک کی بیع جائز نہیں ہے اسلئے مچھلی کی بیع دریا یا تالاب میں جائز نہ ہوگی۔ اور اگر مچھلیاں ایسے گڑھے میں ہوں جس کو دریا یا تالاب سے کاٹ کر باندھ لیا ہو تو اس کی دو سورتیں ہیں ۔ خطیر ہ ایسا چھوٹا ہوگا کہ جس سے بغیر حیلہ کے ہاتھ ڈال کر مچھلیاں پکڑنا ممکن ہو یا اتنا بڑا ہوگا جس سے بغیر حیلہ کے مچھلیاں پکڑ نا ممکن نہ ہو۔ اگر خطیرہ بڑا ہو اور تالاب سے مچھلیاں پکڑ کر اس میں ڈالی ہوں تب بھی اس کی مچھلیوں کا پہنا جائز نہیں ہے کیونکہ یہ مچھلیاں اگر چہ بائع کی مملوک ہیں لیکن غیر مقدور تسلیم ہیں اسلئے ان کی بیع جائز نہ ہوگی۔ اور اگر خطیرہ چھوٹا ہو تو اس کی مچھلیوں کا بیچنا جائز ہے کیونکہ چھوٹے خطیرہ کی مچھلیاں بائع کی مملوک بھی ہیں اور بائع ان کو سپرد کرنے پر قادر بھی ہے۔ اور اگر خطیرہ چھوٹا ہو اور مچھلیاں اس میں خود بخود جمع ہو گئیں اور بائع نے ان کے آنے کا راستہ بھی بند نہیں کیا تو یہ بیچ بھی ناجائز ہے کیونکہ بائع کی طرف سے چونکہ ان کو روکنے اور جمع کرنے میں کوئی عمل نہیں پایا گیا اسلئے اس کی مچھلیاں بالغ کی مملوک نہ ہوں گی ۔ اور غیر ملوک کی بیچ چونکہ نا جائز ہے اسلئے اس خطیرہ کی مچھلیوں کی بیع نا جائز ہے ہاں اگر مچھلیوں کے آنے کا راستہ بند کر دیا اور ان کو بغیر حیلہ کے پکڑ ناممکن ہوا تو بیع جائز ہے۔ فائدہ جن صورتوں میں پانی کے اندر مچھلیاں بیچنا جائز ہے ان صورتوں میں مشتری کو خیار رویت حاصل ہوگا کیونکہ مچھلی کا پانی کے اندر دیکھنا خشکی کے اندر دیکھنے سے متفاوت ہوتا ہے یعنی پانی کے اندر کی رویت خشکی کی رویت کیلئے کافی نہ ہوگی۔
The ruling on selling fish before catching.
He said: It is not permissible to sell fish before catching it, because he sold what he does not own; nor in a pond (hazirah) when it cannot be taken except by catching, because it is not within ability to deliver. And its meaning is when he takes it and throws it into it. And if it can be taken without artifice, it is permissible; except when they have gathered in it by themselves and he has not closed the entrance, due to lack of ownership.
Translation: Quduri said: Selling fish before catching is not permissible, because he sold something he does not own. And in a pond (khalirah/barah) it is not permissible when it is not taken except by hunting, because it is not within his power to deliver. And its meaning is when the buyer caught it and then threw it into the pond. And if it can be caught without artifice, it is permissible; except when the fish have gathered in the pond by themselves and he did not close the entrance (then the sale is not permissible) due to absence of ownership. Explanation: Khalirah is a barah, i.e., a place enclosed for animals with a wooden fence. Here, khalirah means a water pit, because it also forms a barrier for fish from escaping. Hence it is called khalirah. Principally, keep in mind that for the validity of a sale, it is necessary that the sold item be the property of the seller and within his ability to deliver. If the sold item is not the property of the seller, or is owned but not within ability to deliver, the sale will not be valid. The scenario is: selling fish in a river or canal before catching is not permissible. Because as long as the fish is in the river or pond, it is not owned by anyone but is permissible (mubah) - anyone can catch it, and selling what is not owned is not permissible. Therefore, selling fish in a river or pond is not valid. And if the fish are in a pit that has been cut off from the river and enclosed, there are two cases: either the pond is small such that fish can be caught by hand without artifice, or it is so large that catching fish without artifice is not possible. If the pond is large and fish have been caught from the river and thrown into it, then selling its fish is still not permissible because, although the fish are owned by the seller, they are not within ability to deliver, so their sale is not permissible. And if the pond is small, then selling its fish is permissible, because the fish in a small pond are owned by the seller and he is able to deliver them. And if the pond is small and the fish have gathered in it by themselves and the seller did not close the entrance for them, then this sale is also impermissible because no action of prevention or collection is found on the seller's part, so the fish are not his property. And since selling what is not owned is impermissible, the sale of fish in this pond is impermissible. Yes, if he closed the entrance and catching them without artifice became impossible, then the sale is permissible. Benefit: In those cases where selling fish underwater is permissible, the buyer has the option of seeing (khiyar al-ru'yah), because seeing fish underwater is different from seeing on dry land; i.e., underwater sight is not sufficient for dry land sight.
Source pages p. 165

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling from Quduri (matn) on the sale of fish before catching, expanded by the commentator. The core principle is that for a sale to be valid, the item must be owned by the seller (mamluk) and within his ability to deliver (maqdur al-taslim). Selling fish in open water (river, sea) before catching is invalid because they are not owned. In a man-made pond (khalirah), the ruling depends on size and how the fish got there. If the pond is small enough that fish can be caught by hand without artifice, the seller owns them and can deliver, so the sale is valid. If the pond is large so that catching requires artifice (e.g., netting), the fish are not deliverable, so the sale is invalid even if the seller owns them (e.g., he caught them and put them there). Additionally, if fish gather of their own accord in a small pond without any action from the seller (e.g., he didn't close the entrance), he does not own them. The benefit (fa'idah) adds that even in valid sales, the buyer retains the option of seeing (khiyar al-ru'yah) because seeing fish underwater is not equivalent to seeing them out of water.

Key Terms
مقدور التسليم (maqdur al-taslim): Within the seller's ability to deliver the sold item physically to the buyer.
خطیرہ (khalirah): An enclosed pond or pit for fish, either natural or man-made.
خیار رویت (khiyar al-ru'yah): The option to rescind the contract if the item was not seen properly before purchase.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is selling fish in a large pond (khalirah) invalid even if the seller caught and placed them there?
A) Because fish cannot be owned in large ponds.
B) Because the seller cannot deliver them without artifice.
C) Because the buyer did not see them.
D) Because the pond is public property.

Key Takeaway
For a fish sale to be valid in Hanafi fiqh, the fish must be owned by the seller and physically deliverable without extraordinary effort.

Sale of Birds and Unborn Animals: Conditions of Ownership and Delivery
Ruling with proof on bird and fetus sales

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three scenarios of selling a bird and explain why the first two are invalid due to lack of ownership or ability to deliver, and cite the hadith prohibiting the sale of unborn animals.

Core Idea
A sale is invalid if the item is not owned or not deliverable; gharar makes the contract batil.

This lesson examines the sale of birds in various states and the prohibition of selling unborn animals. The Hanafi school emphasizes that for a sale to be valid, the seller must own the item and be able to deliver it. The Prophet's prohibition of selling a fetus (haml) and a fetus of a fetus (habal al-habalah) serves as the primary evidence, with gharar as the underlying rationale.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three scenarios
The passage lists three scenarios for selling a bird: in the air before catching, after catching and releasing, and a bird that comes and goes (e.g., homing pigeon). Distinguish each based on ownership and deliverability.
The third scenario is cut off but implies a possible exception if the bird returns reliably.
2
Apply the ownership condition
Scenario 1: Bird not owned before catching → sale invalid. Scenario 2: Bird owned (caught) but not deliverable after release → sale invalid. Scenario 3: If the bird returns, it may be considered deliverable, but the text does not complete the ruling.
The consensus (bil ittifaq) for the first two scenarios is noted in the commentary.
3
Extend to unborn animals
The sale of a fetus (haml) and a fetus of a fetus (habal al-habalah) is forbidden. The hadith provides the proof, and the underlying cause (illah) is gharar (uncertainty).
Gharar is significant in Hanafi law and invalidates the contract.
4
Trace the dalil
The hadith 'لنهى النبي عن بيع الحمل وحبل الحبلة' is cited. It is ahad (zanni al-thubut) but its meaning is clear (qati al-dalalah) in forbidding such sales due to gharar.
The prohibition is consistent with the principle of avoiding uncertainty in contracts.

The ruling on selling a bird in the air, with it.
He said: And there is no sale of a bird in the air, because it is not owned before being caught; and likewise if he released it from his hand, because it is not within ability to deliver; and there is no sale of a fetus (haml) nor of the offspring (nitaaj), because the Prophet (peace be upon him) forbade the sale of a fetus and the fetus of a fetus (habal al-habalah), and because there is deception (gharar) in it.
Translation: Quduri said: The sale of such a bird that is in the air is not permissible, because it is not owned before being caught; and similarly if he released it from his hand, because it is not within ability to deliver; and the sale of a fetus is not permissible, nor the sale of the fetus of a fetus, because the Prophet (peace be upon him) forbade the sale of a fetus and the fetus of a fetus, and because there is deception in it.
Explanation: There are three scenarios for the sale of a bird:
1. Selling it in the air before catching it.
2. Catching the bird and then releasing it from his hand, then selling it.
3. A bird that comes and goes, like a pigeon that goes away by itself and returns by itself.
In the first two scenarios, by consensus, the sale is invalid. In the first scenario because the bird is not owned, and in the second scenario because... (cut off)

Commentary
This passage presents the ruling on selling birds in various states, from Quduri's matn with commentary. The principle is similar to the fish case: the item must be owned and deliverable. The prohibition also includes selling unborn animals (fetus) because of gharar (uncertainty), based on a hadith.

حمل (haml): The fetus in the womb; selling it is prohibited due to uncertainty of existence and delivery.
حبل الحبلة (habal al-habalah): The fetus of a fetus; a pre-Islamic practice of selling an unborn animal's future offspring.

Conditions for Valid Sale: Ownership and Deliverability
Ruling with conditional scenarios

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two necessary conditions for a valid sale (ownership and deliverability) and apply them to the sale of fish in water, distinguishing the scenarios of khutayrah.

Core Idea
A sale is invalid unless the seller owns the item and can physically deliver it.

The sale of fish in water presents a classic case for testing two fundamental conditions of any valid sale: the seller must own the item and must be able to deliver it. This passage from the Hanafi tradition walks through various scenarios involving fish in natural and artificial enclosures, illustrating how these conditions are applied and what happens when one is missing. Understanding this ruling helps clarify the broader fiqh principles of ownership acquisition and the prohibition of gharar (uncertainty).

Guided Path
1
Identify the two universal conditions for a valid sale
The passage opens by stating that the item must be owned by the seller and capable of delivery. Note that both are required simultaneously.
These conditions are not unique to fish; they apply to all sales.
2
Apply to open water fish (river/pond)
Fish in open water are mubah (res nullius) – not owned by anyone. Therefore, selling them before catching is invalid because the seller lacks ownership.
This is the default position.
3
Analyze the khutayrah (enclosed pit) cases
The pit may be small (deliverable by hand) or large (requires special effort). Ownership depends on whether the seller actively enclosed the fish or merely allowed them to enter.
Small pit + active enclosure = valid; large pit = invalid despite ownership; small pit + passive entry = no ownership.
4
Recognize the khiyar al-ru'yah benefit
In valid sales, the buyer still has the option to annul after seeing the fish on land, because underwater viewing is not equivalent.
This option protects the buyer from deception.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
جواز بیع کیلئے میچ کا بائع کی ملک اور مقدور التسلیم ہونا ضروری ہے اگر مبیع بائع کی ملوک نہ ہو یا مملو تو ہومگر مقدور التسلیم نہ ہو تو بیچ مبیع جائز نہ ہوگی۔ صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ شکار کرنے سے پہلے دریا یا نہر وغیرہ میں مچھلی کا فروخت کرنا جائز نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ مچھلی جب تنگ در پایا تالاب میں ہو تب تک وہ کسی کی ملک نہیں ہوتی بلکہ مباح ہوتی ہے ہر شخص اس کو پکڑ سکتا ہے اور غیر مملوک کی بیع جائز نہیں ہے اسلئے مچھلی کی پیچ در با یا تالاب میں جائز نہ ہوگی۔ اور اگر مچھلیاں ایسے گڑھے میں ہوں جس کو دریا یا تالاب سے کاٹ کر باندھ لیا ہو تو اس کی دو سورتیں ہیں ۔ خطیر ہ ایسا چھوٹا ہوگا کہ جس سے بغیر حیلہ کے ہاتھ ڈال کر مچھلیاں پکڑنا ممکن ہو یا اتنا بڑا ہوگا جس سے بغیر حیلہ کے مچھلیاں پکڑ نا ممکن نہ ہو۔ اگر خطیرہ بڑا ہو اور تالاب سے مچھلیاں پکڑ کر اس میں ڈالی ہوں تب بھی اس کی مچھلیوں کا پہنا جائز نہیں ہے کیونکہ یہ مچھلیاں اگر چہ بائع کی مملوک ہیں لیکن غیر مقدور تسلیم ہیں اسلئے ان کی بیع جائز نہ ہوگی۔ اور اگر خطیرہ چھوٹا ہو تو اس کی مچھلیوں کا بیچنا جائز ہے کیونکہ چھوٹے خطیرہ کی مچھلیاں بائع کی مملوک بھی ہیں اور بائع ان کو سپرد کرنے پر قادر بھی ہے۔ اور اگر خطیرہ چھوٹا ہو اور مچھلیاں اس میں خود بخود جمع ہو گئیں اور بائع نے ان کے آنے کا راستہ بھی بند نہیں کیا تو یہ بیچ بھی ناجائز ہے کیونکہ بائع کی طرف سے چونکہ ان کو روکنے اور جمع کرنے میں کوئی عمل نہیں پایا گیا اسلئے اس کی مچھلیاں بالغ کی مملوک نہ ہوں گی ۔ اور غیر ملوک کی بیچ چونکہ نا جائز ہے اسلئے اس خطیرہ کی مچھلیوں کی بیع نا جائز ہے ہاں اگر مچھلیوں کے آنے کا راستہ بند کر دیا اور ان کو بغیر حیلہ کے پکڑ ناممکن ہوا تو بیع جائز ہے۔ فائدہ جن صورتوں میں پانی کے اندر مچھلیاں بیچنا جائز ہے ان صورتوں میں مشتری کو خیار رویت حاصل ہوگا کیونکہ مچھلی کا پانی کے اندر دیکھنا خشکی کے اندر دیکھنے سے متفاوت ہوتا ہے یعنی پانی کے اندر کی رویت خشکی کی رویت کیلئے کافی نہ ہوگی۔
For a sale to be valid, the merchandise must be owned by the seller and capable of delivery. If the merchandise is not owned by the seller, or even if owned but not capable of delivery, then the sale of the merchandise is not valid. The issue is: selling fish before catching them in a river or canal is not valid. Because when fish are in a river or pond, they are not owned by anyone but are mubah (permissible for anyone to catch), and the sale of non-owned goods is not valid. Therefore, selling fish in a river or pond is not valid. If the fish are in a pit (khutayrah) that has been cut off and enclosed from the river or pond, then there are two possibilities: either it is small enough that fish can be caught by hand without a trick, or it is so large that catching fish without a trick is impossible. If the pit is large and fish are caught from the pond and placed in it, then selling those fish is not valid because even though the fish are owned by the seller, they are not capable of delivery. If the pit is small, selling its fish is valid because the fish are both owned and deliverable. If the pit is small and fish gathered there on their own and the seller did not block their entry, then the sale is invalid because the seller did not perform any act to prevent or collect them, so the fish are not owned by him. The sale of non-owned goods is invalid, so selling fish in such a pit is invalid. However, if he blocked the entry of fish and catching them without a trick is impossible, then the sale is valid. Benefit: In cases where selling fish in water is valid, the buyer has the option of seeing (khiyar al-ru'yah) because seeing fish in water differs from seeing them on dry land, i.e., seeing in water is not sufficient for seeing on land.
Source pages p. 166

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement on the sale of fish in water, explaining the two fundamental conditions for a valid sale: ownership and deliverability. The author differentiates between fish in open water (non-owned, impermissible) and fish in an enclosed pit (khutayrah). For the pit, the size matters: if small and deliverable, sale is valid; if large and not deliverable, invalid. Additionally, if the seller merely allowed fish to enter without active enclosure, ownership is not established. A benefit (fa'idah) is added: when sale is valid, the buyer still has the right to inspect the fish after delivery (khiyar al-ru'yah), as seeing them underwater is not equivalent to seeing them on land. The reasoning is based on the general principle against gharar (uncertainty) and the need for the seller to have both ownership and ability to deliver.

Key Terms
خطیرہ (khutayrah): A small pond or artificial enclosure made by cutting off a section of a river or pond.
مقدور التسلیم (maqdur al-taslim): The ability of the seller to deliver the sold item physically to the buyer.
خیار رویت (khiyar al-ru'yah): The buyer's option to annul the sale after seeing the item if it does not meet expectations, granted when the item was not seen before purchase.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Always, regardless of how the fish got there.
B) Only if the fish are owned and deliverable, and the seller actively enclosed them.
C) Only if the fish are from a large pit.
D) Only if the fish are caught before sale.

Key Takeaway
A sale of fish in water is valid only when the fish are both owned by the seller (through active acquisition) and physically deliverable.

Selling Birds in the Air: Three Scenarios
Ruling on three scenarios of selling birds

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three scenarios for selling birds in the air and apply the conditions of ownership and deliverability to determine the validity of the sale.

Core Idea
A sale requires both ownership and deliverability; if either is missing, the sale is invalid.

You may think that owning a bird is enough to sell it. But Islamic law also requires that you be able to deliver it. This lesson presents three scenarios from al-Quduri's matn that illustrate this principle: a bird in the air, a bird caught then released, and a bird that habitually returns. Understanding these will help you grasp the foundational conditions of a valid sale.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two conditions for a valid sale
In Hanafi fiqh, a sale requires the seller to own the item and be able to hand it over. The text emphasizes these conditions with the ruling on birds.
The daleel for this is the prohibition of gharar.
2
Analyze the first scenario: bird in the air before capture
The bird is not owned, so the sale fails on the first condition (ownership).
This is the clearest case of non-ownership.
3
Analyze the second scenario: bird caught then released
The bird was owned after capture, but upon release, deliverability is lost. The sale fails on the second condition (deliverability).
This shows that ownership alone is insufficient.
4
Analyze the third scenario: bird that comes and goes
If catching the bird is impossible without a trick (i.e., it habitually returns), then deliverability is possible and the sale is valid. Otherwise, it is invalid.
This is a conditional exception based on reliable return.
5
Understand the role of gharar
The underlying rationale is that uncertainty (gharar) invalidates the sale. The hadith about selling fetuses and the principle of gharar are cited to support the ruling.
The text also transitions to the ruling on selling fetuses, covered separately.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
جو پرندہ ہوا میں مع اس کی بیع کا حکم قال ولا بيع الطير في الهواء لانه غير مملوك قبل الاخذ وكذا لوارسله من يده لأنه غير مقدور التسليم ولا بيع الحمل ولا النتاج لنهى النبي عن بيع الحمل وحبل الحبلة ولان فيه غررا ترجمہ قدوری نے کہا اور ایسے پرند کی بیع جائز نہیں ہے جو ہوا میں ہو کیونکہ وہ پکڑا جانے سے پہلے غیر مملوک ہے اور ایسے ہی اگر اس کو اپنے ہاتھ سے چھوڑ دیا ہو کیونکہ وہ غیر مقدور تسلیم ہے اور نہ عمل کی بیع جائز ہے اور نہ حمل کے عمل کی کیونکہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے حمل اور حمل کے حمل کی بیچ سے منع فرمایا ہے اور اسلئے کہ اس میں دھوکا ہے۔ تشریح پرندے کی بیچ کی تین صورتیں ہیں۔ - شکار کرنے سے پہلے ہوا میں بیچنا۔ ۲۔ پرندے کا شکار کر کے اس کو اپنے ہاتھ سے چھوڑ دیا پھر اس کو فروخت کر دیا۔ ۳۔ پرندہ آتا جاتا ہے جیسے کبوتر کہ خود چلا جاتا ہے اور خود ہی آجاتا ہے۔ پہلی دو صورتوں میں بالا تفاق بیع نا جائز ہے۔ پہلی صورت میں پرندے کے غیر مملوک ہونے کی وجہ سے اور دوسری صورت میں غیر مقدور التسلیم ہونے کی وجہ سے کیونکہ دوسری صورت میں شکار کرنے کی وجہ سے پرندہ بائع کا ملک تو ہو گیا مگر چھوڑ دینے کی وجہ سے غیر مقدور تسلیم ہو گیا ہے اور تیسری صورت میں اگر پرندہ کا بغیر حیلہ کے پکڑ ناممکن ہوا تو اس کی بیع جائز ہے ورنہ نہیں۔
The ruling on selling a bird in the air. He (al-Quduri) said: The sale of a bird in the air is not valid because it is not owned before capture. Similarly, if he releases it from his hand, (the sale is not valid) because it is not capable of delivery. And the sale of al-haml (fetus) and al-nataj (offspring of fetus) is not valid due to the Prophet's prohibition of selling al-haml and habl al-habalah, and because there is gharar (deception) in it. Translation: Al-Quduri said: The sale of a bird that is in the air is not valid because it is not owned before capture. Similarly, if he releases it from his hand, because it is not capable of delivery. And the sale of al-haml and al-nataj is not valid because the Prophet (peace be upon him) prohibited selling al-haml and habl al-habalah, and because there is gharar in it. Commentary: There are three scenarios for selling a bird: 1) Selling it in the air before capture. 2) Catching the bird and then releasing it from his hand, then selling it. 3) A bird that comes and goes, like a pigeon that flies away and returns on its own. In the first two scenarios, the sale is unanimously invalid. In the first scenario, due to non-ownership; in the second, due to non-deliverability, because in the second scenario the bird became owned by the seller due to capture, but then became non-deliverable due to release. In the third scenario, if catching the bird without a trick is impossible, the sale is valid; otherwise, it is not.
Source pages p. 166

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling statement on the sale of birds, distinguishing three scenarios. The core principle is that a sale requires both ownership and the ability to deliver. The first scenario (bird free in the air) fails because of non-ownership. The second (bird caught then released) fails because although owned, it cannot be delivered. The third scenario involves a bird that habitually returns (like a homing pigeon); the sale is valid only if it is impossible to catch without a trick, implying some form of deliverability. The ruling is derived from the general prohibition of gharar (deception) and the explicit hadith about selling fetuses. The text also transitions to the ruling on selling fetuses, which is covered in the next lesson.

Key Terms
طیر (tayr): Bird; in this context, any bird that may be caught or released.
غرر (gharar): Deception or uncertainty in a transaction that may lead to dispute.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is selling a bird that was caught and then released by the seller invalid in the Hanafi school?
A) Because the bird was not owned.
B) Because the bird is not capable of delivery.
C) Because the sale of birds is always invalid.
D) Because the bird is considered public property.

Key Takeaway
A sale is valid only if the seller owns the object and can deliver it; selling a bird in the air or after releasing it is invalid due to lack of one of these conditions.

Selling the Fetus and Offspring of Fetus: Prohibition and Proof
Ruling on selling the unborn fetus and the offspring of the fetus with hadith proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling on selling the unborn fetus and its future offspring, and identify the two proofs (hadith and gharar) that render the sale batil.

Core Idea
The sale of an unborn fetus or its future offspring is void due to explicit prophetic prohibition and inherent uncertainty (gharar).

This passage addresses a specific pre-Islamic practice of selling unborn animals and their future offspring. The Hanafi school, relying on a hadith from Ibn Umar and the principle of gharar (excessive uncertainty), declares such transactions completely invalid (batil). Understanding this ruling helps you grasp how Islamic law protects contractual clarity and prevents exploitation through ambiguity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two prohibited sales
The text distinguishes between selling the unborn fetus (al-haml) and selling the future offspring of that fetus (al-nataj or habl al-habalah). Recognize the concrete examples given (e.g., buying a calf in the womb; buying the future calf of that calf).
The latter (al-nataj) is even more uncertain.
2
Locate the first proof: the hadith
The author cites the hadith: 'The Prophet (PBUH) prohibited the sale of al-madamin, al-malaqih, and habl al-habalah.' Understand that 'habl al-habalah' refers to the offspring of an unborn fetus.
The hadith is the primary nas-based evidence.
3
Locate the second proof: gharar
The text explains that selling an unborn animal involves gharar because it is unknown whether the fetus exists or will be born safely. The Prophet also prohibited gharar transactions generically.
Gharar undermines mutual consent and validity.
4
Determine the ruling level
Combining the explicit prohibition (nahy) and the presence of gharar, the sale is not merely invalid (fasid) but void (batil) from its inception. There is no way to rectify it.
In Hanafi law, nahy in transactions typically leads to fasād or butlān; here it is butlān.
5
Confirm cross-madhhab agreement
The text implies consensus: all major schools prohibit such sales for the same reasons. This strengthens the confidence in the ruling.
The ruling is muttafaq alayh.

ولا بيع الحمل ولا النتاج لنهى النبي عن بيع الحمل وحبل الحبلة ولان فيه غررا ... تشریح ... اور حمل یعنی جنین اور حمل کے حمل کی بیع نا جائز ہے۔ حمل کی بیچ کی صورت یہ ہے کہ مثلا مشتری نے کہا کہ اس اونٹنی یا بکری کے پیٹ میں جو بچہ ہے ایک سورو پیہ میں میں نے خرید لیا بائع نے اس کو قبول کر لیا۔ اور نتاج یعنی حمل کے حمل کی بیع یہ ہے کہ مشتری نے کہا کہ اس اونٹنی کے پیٹ میں اگر مادہ بچہ ہوتو یہ مادہ بچہ بڑا ہو کر جو بچہ دے گا میں نے اس کو خرید لیا بائع نے اس کو قبول کر لیا۔ زمانہ جاہلیت میں یہ عادت تھی کہ ایک آدمی دوسرے سے اونٹنی خرید تا اس شرط پر کہ یہ اونٹنی میرے پاس اس وقت تک رہے گی جب تک کہ یہ بچہ جنے پھر اس بچہ کے بچہ پیدا ہو پس جب اس اونٹنی کے بچہ سے بچہ پیدا ہو جاتا تو یہ انٹی بائع کو واپس کر دی جاتی اور یہ انٹی بائع کی ملک ہو جاتی تھی ۔ رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے اس بیع کو باطل قرار دیا اور حمل اور حمل کے حمل کی بیج سے منع فرمایا۔ چنانچہ ابن عمر کی روایت ہے ان النبی صلى الله عليه وسلم نھی عن بيع المضامين والملاقيح و حبل الحبلة - مضامین مضمون کی جمع ہے جو نر جانوروں کے صاب میں ہو اس کو مضمون کہتے ہیں۔ ملقوح کی جمع ہے جو رحم مادر میں ہوتا ہے اس کو ملقوح کہتے ہیں۔ بہر حال نہیں رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم کی وجہ سے ان کی بیع نا جائز ہے۔ دوسری دلیل یہ ہے کہ اس بیع میں دھوکا ہے کیونکہ معلوم نہیں کہ پیٹ میں کچھ ہے یا یونہی ہوا کی وجہ سے پھولا ہوا ہے اور دھوکہ کی بیع سے رسول اکرم صلى الله عليه وسلم نے منع فرمایا ہے۔ اسلئے یہ بیع ممنوع ہوگی۔
And the sale of al-haml (fetus) and al-nataj (offspring of fetus) is not valid due to the Prophet's prohibition of selling al-haml and habl al-habalah, and because there is gharar in it. ... Commentary: And al-haml, i.e., the fetus, and the sale of the fetus's offspring is invalid. The form of selling al-haml is that, for example, the buyer says, 'I have bought the offspring in the belly of this she-camel or goat for one hundred dirhams,' and the seller accepts. Al-nataj, i.e., selling the offspring of the fetus, is that the buyer says, 'If the offspring in the belly of this she-camel is female, then I buy the offspring that this female will give birth to after it grows up,' and the seller accepts. In the time of Jahiliyyah, it was customary for a man to buy a she-camel on the condition that it would remain with him until it gave birth, and then until the offspring's offspring was born. Then when the offspring's offspring was born, the she-camel would be returned to the seller, and the she-camel would become the seller's property. The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) declared this sale void and prohibited selling al-haml and habl al-habalah. Thus, Ibn Umar narrates that the Prophet (peace be upon him) prohibited the sale of al-madamin, al-malaqih, and habl al-habalah. Madamin is the plural of maddamun, which is what is in the loins of male animals; malaqih is the plural of mulaqqah, which is what is in the womb. In any case, due to the Prophet's prohibition, their sale is invalid. The second proof is that there is gharar in this sale, because it is not known whether there is something in the belly or it is just bloated with wind, and the Prophet prohibited the sale of gharar. Therefore, this sale is prohibited.
Source pages p. 166

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof regarding the sale of unborn fetuses (al-haml) and the future offspring of an unborn fetus (al-nataj or habl al-habalah). The author provides two proofs: first, an explicit hadith from Ibn Umar prohibiting the sale of al-madamin, al-malaqih, and habl al-habalah. Second, the presence of gharar (uncertainty) because the existence and condition of the fetus are unknown. The commentary explains the Jahili practice that led to this prohibition. The Hanafi ruling is that such sales are void (batil) due to these proofs. The hadith is cited as evidence that the transaction is impermissible in any form.

Key Terms
حمل (haml): The unborn fetus in the womb of an animal.
نتاج (nataj): The offspring of the fetus; the future offspring of an unborn animal.
حبل الحبلة (habl al-habalah): The offspring of the fetus; a pre-Islamic practice of selling the future offspring of an unborn animal.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The Quranic verse on fair trade.
B) The Prophet's prohibition of selling al-madamin, al-malaqih, and habl al-habalah.
C) The consensus of the Companions.
D) The principle of qiyas on selling dates on trees.

Key Takeaway
The sale of an unborn fetus or its future offspring is void (batil) due to explicit hadith prohibition and the principle of gharar.

Selling Milk in the Udder: Prohibition Due to Gharar
Ruling with three proofs on the prohibition of selling milk in the udder.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on selling milk in the udder and explain the three reasons for its prohibition based on gharar.

Core Idea
Selling milk in the udder is batil because gharar exists in the milk's presence, quantity, and separation.

In this lesson, we examine a key ruling from al-Quduri's Mukhtasar: the prohibition of selling milk while it is still in the udder. The author provides three distinct proofs, all rooted in the prohibition of gharar. Understanding these reasons clarifies the Hanafi emphasis on certainty in transactions.

Guided Path
1
State the ruling and its hukm level
Identify the transaction and its legal classification according to the Hanafi school. The sale of milk in the udder is declared batil (void).
The ruling is from the matn of al-Quduri.
2
Examine the first form of gharar
The udder may be swollen with wind rather than milk, so the object may not actually exist as sold.
This is gharar in existence (wujud).
3
Examine the second form of gharar
There will be dispute about the method of milking: the buyer wants every drop, the seller wants some left. This leads to potential conflict (mufdi ila al-niza').
This is gharar in quantity (qadr).
4
Examine the third form of gharar
During milking, new milk is secreted, mixing the sold milk with unsold new milk, making separation impossible.
This is gharar in separability (tamayyuz).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
دودھ کی تھنوں میں بیچ کا حکم قال ولا اللبن فى الضرع للغرر فعساه انتفاخ ولا نه ينازع فى كيفية الحلب وربما يزداد فيختلط المبيع بغيره ترجمہ اور تھن کے دودھ کا بیچنا بھی جائز نہیں ہے کیونکہ (اس میں ) دھوکا ہے اسلئے کہ ہو سکتا ہے کہ تھن ریاح سے پھولا ہو اور اسلئے کہ دو ہنے کی کیفیت میں جھگڑا ہوگا اور بسا اوقات دودھ زیادہ اترتا ہے تو مبیع غیر مبیع کے ساتھ مل جائے گی۔ تشریح مسئلہ تھن کے دودھ کا فروخت کرنا نا جائز ہے۔ دلیل اول ... کیونکہ اس میں دھوکہ ہے اور دھو کہ اس وجہ سے ہے کہ ممکن ہے کہ تھی ریاح کی وجہ سے پھولا ہو ۔ مشتری اس کو دودھ خیال کرے حالانکہ اس میں دودھ نہیں بلکہ ریاح ہے۔ اور دھوکہ کی بیع سے مدنی آقا صلى الله عليه وسلم نے منع فرمایا ہے۔ اسلئے تھن کے دودھ کی بیچ نا جائز ہے۔ دوسری دلیل یہ ہے کہ دو ہنے کی کیفیت میں جھگڑا ہوگا۔ مشتری چاہے گا کہ ایک ایک قطرہ نچوڑ لوں اور بائع کی آرزو ہوگی کہ تھنوں میں کچھ باقی رہنا چاہئے اور مفضی الی النزاع بھی عدم جواز بیع کی دلیل ہے۔ تیسری دلیل یہ ہے کہ دودھ تھنوں میں قطرہ قطرہ اکٹھا ہوتا ہے۔ پس تھنوں کا دودھ بیچنے اور اس کو نکالنے کے درمیان بھی کچھ نہ کچھ دودھ پیدا ہوگا اور بیچنے کے بعد جو دودھ تھنوں میں پیدا ہوا ہے وہ غیر صحیح ہے اس کا مالک بائع ہے اور جو دودھ بیچتے وقت تھنوں میں موجود تھا وہ صبیح ہے۔ اس کا مالک مشتری ہے اور یہ دونوں یعنی بیع اور غیر مبیع اس طرح مل گئے کہ ایک کو دوسرے سے علیحدہ کرنا متعذر ہے۔ اور مبیع کا۔
The ruling on selling milk in the udder. He (al-Quduri) said: And not the milk in the udder due to gharar, for perhaps it is a swelling (due to wind), and because there would be dispute regarding the method of milking, and sometimes milk increases and the sold item mixes with other. Translation: And the sale of milk in the udder is not valid because there is deception (gharar) in it. This is because it is possible that the udder is swollen from wind (not milk), and because there will be dispute about the method of milking, and sometimes more milk comes out so the sold item mixes with other. Commentary: The issue: selling milk in the udder is invalid. First proof: because there is gharar, and the reason for gharar is that it is possible the udder is swollen due to wind; the buyer thinks it is milk, but there is no milk, only wind. The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) prohibited the sale of gharar. Therefore, selling milk in the udder is invalid. Second proof: there will be dispute about the method of milking; the buyer wants to extract every drop, while the seller wants some to remain; and a thing that leads to dispute is a proof against its permissibility. Third proof: milk collects drop by drop in the udder; between the sale and the extraction, some additional milk will be produced. The milk produced after the sale is non-sold (ghayr mabi') and belongs to the seller, while the milk present at the time of sale is the sold item (mabi') and belongs to the buyer. These two mix in such a way that separating them is impossible; thus the mabi' becomes unknown.
Source pages p. 167

Commentary
This passage provides a ruling with multiple proofs on the impermissibility of selling milk in the udder (al-laban fi al-dar'). The author gives three reasons, each based on the principle that gharar (deception or uncertainty) invalidates a sale. First, the udder may be swollen from wind rather than milk, so the buyer is deceived. Second, the method of milking will cause dispute because the buyer wants all the milk while the seller wants some left. Third, additional milk is secreted during the milking process, causing mixing of the sold milk and the unsold new milk, which cannot be separated. The hadith prohibition of gharar is cited as the primary evidence. This ruling emphasizes the Hanafi concern for certainty in transactions.

Key Terms
ضرع (dar'): The udder of a female animal containing milk.
غرر (gharar): Deception or uncertainty in a transaction that leads to potential dispute or harm.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is NOT a reason given in the text for prohibiting the sale of milk in the udder?
A) The udder may be swollen with wind instead of milk.
B) There will be a dispute about the method of milking.
C) The milk may be contaminated with blood.
D) New milk may be secreted, causing mixing of sold and unsold milk.

Key Takeaway
Selling milk in the udder is batil because gharar exists in the milk's presence, quantity, and separability, all leading to potential dispute.

Sale of Wool on the Back is Invalid: Hanafi Ruling and Proofs
Ruling on selling wool while on the animal

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on selling wool on the back of a sheep and explain the textual and rational proofs that invalidate it, including the intra-Hanafi dispute.

Core Idea
Selling wool on the back is haram due to uncertainty, mixing, and explicit prohibition.

This passage addresses a specific transaction: selling wool while it is still attached to a sheep or goat. The Hanafi ruling is that such a sale is invalid. The text provides multiple lines of reasoning—attributive nature of wool, growth pattern causing mixing, inevitable dispute over cutting—and cites a prophetic prohibition. It also notes an intra-Hanafi disagreement, with Imam Abu Yusuf reportedly allowing it, though the relied-upon position is prohibition. Understanding this ruling sharpens your ability to identify gharar (uncertainty) in sales.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is selling wool on the back of a sheep or goat. The ruling is that it is not permissible (haram/batil). Note that the text begins 'He said: And not the wool on the back…'.
2
Examine the rational proofs (‘illal)
The text gives three reasons: (1) wool is an attribute (wasf) of the animal, not an independent property; (2) it grows from below, so new wool mixes with the sold wool; (3) the cut is indeterminate, leading to dispute (niza‘). Contrast with branches (grow from above) and green crop (can be uprooted).
These proofs show why the sale is invalid on logical grounds.
3
Locate the dalil naqli
The hadith: 'He prohibited the sale of wool on the back of sheep, milk in the udder, and ghee in milk.' This is an explicit textual prohibition. Identify the type: ahad hadith, zanni al-thubut and dalala, but sufficient to establish prohibition in Hanafi usul.
The hadith is the primary proof, reinforced by rational reasons.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
The text states the hadith is a proof against Abu Yusuf, who reportedly allowed the sale. This is a minority view within the school. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is the prohibition held by Abu Hanifa and Muhammad al-Shaybani.
Understand that even within a school, there can be ikhtilaf, but the majority and strongest position is followed.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The tarjih (preference) is based on the explicit hadith and the rational proofs (gharar, niza‘). Abu Yusuf's view is outweighed. The practical consequence: a sale of wool on the back is void; a judge would not enforce it.
The thamarah al-khilaf: different rulings lead to different legal outcomes.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال ولا الصوف على ظهر الغنم لانه من اوصاف الحيوان ولا نه ينبت من اسفل فيختلط المبيع بغيره بخلاف القوائم لا نها تزيد من اعلى وبخلاف القصيل لانه يمكن قلعه والقطع فى الصوف متعين فيقع التنازع في موضع القطع وقد صح انه نهى عن بيع الصوف على ظهر الغنم وعن لبن في ضرع وسمن في لبن وهو حجة على ابى يوسف فى هذا الصوف حيث جوز بيعه فيما يروى عنه ترجمہ قدوری نے کہا اور بکری کی پیٹھ پر اون خرید نا بھی جائز نہیں ہے اسلئے کہ اون حیوان کے اوصاف میں سے ہے اور اسلئے کہ وہ نیچے سے اگتی ہے پس مبیع کا اختلاط غیر مبیع سے ہو جائے گا۔ برخلاف درخت کی شاخوں کے کیونکہ وہ اوپر سے بڑھتی ہیں اور برخلاف سبز کھیتی کے اسلئے کہ اس کا اکھاڑ لیا ممکن ہے اور اون میں کا نامتعین ہے اسلئے کاٹنے کی جگہ میں جھگڑا پیدا ہوگا۔ اور صحیح طور پر یہ ثابت ہے کہ بکری کی پیٹھ پر اون بیچنے اور تھن میں دودھ بیچنے اور دودھ میں بھی بیچنے سے منع فرمایا ہے۔ اور یہ حدیث امام ابو یوسف کے خلاف حجت ہے ان سے روایت کیا جاتا ہے کہ انہوں نے اس کی بیع جائز کہا ہے۔
He said: 'And not the wool on the back of the sheep, because it is among the attributes of the animal, and because it grows from below, so the sold item mixes with other. Unlike branches, because they increase from above, and unlike green crop, because it can be uprooted. And cutting the wool is determinate, so dispute occurs about the place of cutting. And it is authentically established that he forbade the sale of wool on the back of sheep, and milk in the udder, and ghee in milk. And this is a proof against Abu Yusuf in this wool, as he permitted its sale in what is narrated from him.' Translation of Urdu: Quduri said: And buying wool on the back of a goat is also not permissible because wool is among the attributes of the animal, and because it grows from below, so the sold item will mix with unsold. Unlike tree branches, because they grow from above, and unlike green crop, because it can be uprooted. And in wool, cutting is determinate, so dispute arises about the place of cutting. And it is authentically established that he forbade the sale of wool on the back of sheep, and milk in the udder, and ghee in milk. And this hadith is evidence against Imam Abu Yusuf, for it is narrated from him that he permitted its sale.
Source pages p. 168

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof (hukm wa dalil) concerning the sale of wool while still on the back of a sheep or goat (al-suf 'ala zahr al-ghanam). The ruling is that it is not permissible. The text provides several reasons: first, wool is an attribute (wasf) of the animal, and attributes are not independently saleable. Second, it grows from below, meaning that after sale, new wool grows at the base, mixing with the sold wool in a way that cannot be separated, invalidating the sale. The text contrasts this with tree branches (which grow from above, so new growth is on top and belongs to the buyer) and green crop (which can be uprooted entirely, avoiding dispute). Third, there is dispute over where to cut the wool (whether close to the skin or leaving some). This leads to niza', which invalidates the sale. Additionally, the text mentions a hadith that explicitly forbids such sales. Importantly, the text notes that this hadith is a proof against Imam Abu Yusuf, who reportedly allowed the sale of wool on the back. This indicates an intra-Hanafi dispute: the relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that it is invalid, based on the hadith and the reasoning of mixing and dispute.

Key Terms
صوف (suf): Wool on the back of sheep or goats; a part of the animal's body.
قوائم (qawa'im): Branches of a tree (as a contrast case showing permissible sale).
قصیل (qasil): Green crop (like fodder) that can be uprooted entirely.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because wool grows from below, and new growth after sale cannot be separated from the sold wool.
B) Because the buyer and seller always argue about the price.
C) Because the wool is often dirty.
D) Because the animal might die before shearing.

Key Takeaway
The sale of wool on the back of a sheep is invalid due to gharar (uncertainty over cutting), inevitable mixing, and an explicit prophetic prohibition.

Selling Wool on the Back: Invalid Due to Inseparable Mixing
Ruling with proof and intra-Hanafi dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on selling wool on the back of an animal and explain why the mixing of growth invalidates the sale, while distinguishing it from permissible cases like selling tree branches.

Core Idea
Selling wool while still on the animal is invalid because it grows from below, creating inseparable mixing that leads to dispute.

This passage from Quduri's matn, with commentary from Al-Hidayah, addresses a specific sale: wool on the back of a sheep. The ruling is batil (void) due to two key reasons: wool is a description (wasf) of the animal, and it grows from below, causing new growth to mix with the sold wool inseparably. The passage contrasts this with permissible sales of tree branches and green crops, and also presents an intra-Hanafi dispute where Imam Abu Yusuf reportedly allowed it. Understanding this ruling sharpens your ability to apply the principle that anything leading to uncertainty and dispute invalidates a sale.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling and Its Basis
State the Hanafi position: selling wool on the back is not permissible (batil). Note the two reasons: wool is a description (wasf) and grows from below causing mixing.
The text also cites a hadith prohibiting such a sale.
2
Understand the Mixing Argument (Ikhtilat)
Wool grows from below (as proven by the dye test). After sale, new growth at the base is non-sold and becomes inseparably mixed with the sold portion. This ikhtilat invalidates the sale.
This is the core illa (effective cause) for the ruling.
3
Examine the Contrasting Cases
Compare with tree branches (grow from above, so new growth belongs to buyer) and green crop (can be uprooted entirely, avoiding dispute). These cases are permissible because no problematic mixing occurs.
The contrasts highlight the specific reason for invalidity.
4
Analyze the Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Imam Abu Yusuf reportedly permitted the sale, arguing wool is beneficial and deliverable. The passage rebuts this with the hadith: the Prophet (peace be upon him) forbade such sales. The hadith overrides general permissibility.
The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is impermissibility.
5
Determine the Practical Consequence
A Hanafi today cannot execute a contract for wool on a live animal. If done, the contract is void. Wool must be sold after shearing when it is a separate, measurable commodity.
This is the thamarah al-khilaf (practical difference) from the dispute.

قال ولا الصوف على ظهر العم لانه من اوصاف الحيوان ولا نه ينبت من اسفل فيختلط المبيع بغيره بخلاف القوائم لا نها تزيد من اعلى وبخلاف القصيل لانه يمكن قلعه والقطع فى الصوف متعين فيقع التنازع في موضع القطع وقد صح انه نهى عن بيع الصوف على ظهر الغنم وعن لبن في ضرع وسمن في لبن وهو حجة على ابى يوسف فى هذا الصوف حيث جوز بيعه فيما يروى عنه
ترجمہ قدوری نے کہا اور بکری کی پیٹھ پر اون خرید نا بھی جائز نہیں ہے اسلئے کہ اون حیوان کے اوصاف میں سے ہے اور اسلئے کہ وہ نیچے سے اگتی ہے پس مبیع کا اختلاط غیر مبیع سے ہو جائے گا۔ برخلاف درخت کی شاخوں کے کیونکہ وہ اوپر سے بڑھتی ہیں اور برخلاف سبز کھیتی کے اسلئے کہ اس کا اکھاڑ لیا ممکن ہے اور اون میں کا نامتعین ہے اسلئے کاٹنے کی جگہ میں جھگڑا پیدا ہوگا۔ اور صحیح طور پر یہ ثابت ہے کہ بکری کی پیٹھ پر اون بیچنے اور تھن میں دودھ بیچنے اور دودھ میں بھی بیچنے سے منع فرمایا ہے۔ اور یہ حدیث امام ابو یوسف کے خلاف حجت ہے ان سے روایت کیا جاتا ہے کہ انہوں نے اس کی بیع جائز کہا ہے۔
تشریح مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ بکری اور بھیٹر کی پیٹھ پر اون کا فروخت کرنا جائز نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ اس کو کاٹنے سے پہلے وہ حیوان کے اوصاف میں سے ہے اور اوصاف تابع ہوتے ہیں اور تابع چونکہ مال غیر متقوم ہوتا ہے۔ اسلئے بغیر متبوع کے اس کی بیع جائز نہ ہوگی ۔ دوسری دلیل یہ ہے کہ اون نیچے سے اگتی ہے اور اس کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ بکری کی پیٹھ پر اگر اون کو رنگ دیا گیا اور کچھ دن کیلئے اسکو چھوڑ دیا گیا تو اون کا اوپر والا حصہ رنگا ر ہے گا اور بالوں کی جڑیں اس رنگ میں رنگی ہو ئیں نہ ہوں گی۔ اس سے معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ اون نیچے سے اگتی ہے۔ پس پیٹھ پر اون فروخت کرنے کے بعد اور کاٹنے سے پہلے اور میں جس حصہ کا اضافہ ہو گا فروخت کرنا نا جائز اور باطل ہے۔ ہاں درخت کی شاخوں کا درخت پر بیچنا جائز ہے۔ کیونکہ درخت کی شاخیں اوپر سے بڑھتی نہیں اور دلیل اس کی یہ ہے کہ درخت کے تنے کے کسی حصہ پر اگر دھاگہ باندھ کر کچھ دنوں کیلئے اسلئے بکری کی پیٹھ پر اون کی بیع نا جائز ہے۔ اور بالیاں نکلنے سے پہلے سبز کھیتی کی بیع جائز ہے۔ صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ بکری کی پیٹھ پر اون بیچنا جائز ہے کیونکہ اون المنتجوم منتف به او مقدور تسلیم ہے اور جو چیز مال متقوم منقع بہ مقدور تسلیم ہواس کی بیع جائز ہوتی ہے اسلئے بکری کی پشت پر ون کی بینچ جائز ہے مگر حدیث مذکور امام ابو یوسف کے خلاف حجت ہے۔
He said: And [it is not permissible to sell] wool on the back of a goat/sheep because it is among the descriptions of the animal, and because it grows from below, so the sold item mixes with others, unlike branches because they grow from above, and unlike green crop because it can be uprooted. Cutting the wool is determined, so dispute occurs at the place of cutting. It is authentically reported that he forbade selling wool on the back of sheep, milk in the udder, and ghee in milk, and this is evidence against Abu Yusuf regarding this wool, where he permitted its sale according to what is narrated from him. Translation: Quduri said: And buying wool on the back of a goat is also not permissible because wool is among the descriptions of the animal, and because it grows from below, so the sold item mixes with others. Unlike tree branches because they grow from above, and unlike green crop because it can be uprooted. In wool, the cutting place is indeterminate, so dispute arises over the place of cutting. It is authentically proven that he forbade selling wool on the back of a goat, milk in the udder, and ghee in milk. This hadith is evidence against Imam Abu Yusuf; it is narrated from him that he permitted its sale. Commentary: The issue is that selling wool on the back of a goat or sheep is not permissible because before cutting it is among the descriptions of the animal, and descriptions are subsidiary, and the subsidiary is non-valuable property, so its sale without the principal is not permissible. A second proof is that wool grows from below; evidence is that if the wool on a goat's back is dyed and left for days, the upper part will be dyed but the roots will not be dyed, showing it grows from below. After selling wool on the back and before cutting, any new growth is non-sold and mixes with the sold item inseparably. When the sold item mixes with non-sold in such a way, the sale becomes void. Therefore selling wool on the back of a goat or sheep is impermissible and void. However, selling tree branches on the tree is permissible because branches grow from above; evidence is that if a thread is tied around a tree trunk and left, after days the thread remains at the same distance, showing branches grow from above. The upper part is owned by the buyer, so new growth is in the buyer's ownership, and no mixing occurs. Similarly, selling green crop before ears appear is permissible because it can be uprooted without dispute, whereas wool's cutting place is indeterminate, leading to dispute. The author of Hidayah says that selling wool on the back of a goat is permissible because wool is beneficial and deliverable, and any beneficial, valuable property that is deliverable can be sold; but the mentioned hadith is evidence against Abu Yusuf.
Source pages p. 168

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof and an intra-madhhab dispute. The matn from Quduri states that selling wool on the back of a sheep or goat is not permissible. The reason is twofold: (1) wool is a description (wasf) of the animal, and descriptions are subsidiary non-valuable property (mal ghayr mutaqawwim) when sold without the principal; (2) wool grows from below, meaning after sale, new growth occurs at the base, mixing with the sold wool in a way that cannot be separated. The text contrasts this with tree branches, which grow from above, so new growth belongs to the buyer and no mixing occurs; and with green crop, which can be uprooted entirely, avoiding dispute over the cutting point. The hadith prohibition is cited as evidence: the Prophet forbade selling wool on the back, milk in the udder, and ghee in milk. This hadith is used against Imam Abu Yusuf, who reportedly permitted selling wool on the back. The commentary elaborates on the growth direction using the dye test and the thread test, and explains that the mixing invalidates the sale. The author of Hidayah is quoted as saying it is permissible because wool is beneficial and deliverable, but the hadith is presented as overriding evidence. Thus the relied-upon position (al-mufta bihi) is impermissibility, following the majority of the Hanafi school and the explicit hadith.

Key Terms
الصوف (al-suf): Wool on the back of a sheep or goat, considered a description (wasf) of the animal before shearing.
اختلاط (ikhtilat): Mixing of the sold item with a non-sold item in a way that separation is impossible, making the sale void.
مبيع (mabi'): The item being sold.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the primary reason for the invalidity of selling wool on the back of a sheep?
A) The wool is not considered property.
B) The wool grows from below and mixes with non-sold new growth.
C) The animal might die before delivery.
D) The hadith says it is makruh (disliked).

Key Takeaway
Selling wool on the back of an animal is invalid in the Hanafi school due to inseparable mixing of sold and non-sold growth, supported by hadith.

Buyu — Sales and Trade
intermediate
8 min
Selling a Fixed Beam or a Yard of Cloth: Harm and Invalidity
States ruling with reasoning and exception

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on selling a beam in a ceiling or a yard of cloth, identify the reasons for invalidity (darar and jahl), and apply the exception rule when the seller separates the item before cancellation.

Core Idea
A sale is invalid if delivery requires harming the remaining property, unless the seller removes the harm before cancellation.

In this passage, we examine a specific ruling from the Hanafi school regarding the sale of a beam that is part of a ceiling or a yard of cloth from a larger piece. The key legal issue is whether such sales are valid when delivery inevitably causes harm to the remaining property. The text clarifies the ruling, provides reasoning, and discusses an interesting exception that can cure the initial invalidity. We will also compare this with the sale of openly divisible items like silver and distinguish it from hidden items like pits in dates.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two prohibited sales
The text covers two cases: selling a beam already fixed in a ceiling, and selling a specific yard of cloth from a stitched piece. Note that the sale is prohibited regardless of whether the parties mention cutting or not.
The prohibition is not due to lack of specification but due to the necessity of harm.
2
Understand the reason: harm (darar)
The core reason for invalidity is that delivery cannot be made without causing harm to the remaining property. For the beam, removing it damages the ceiling; for the cloth, cutting it damages the remaining fabric. The contract does not obligate the seller to cause harm.
This is based on the maxim 'لا ضرر ولا ضرار' (no harm and no reciprocating harm).
3
Contrast with the silver example
The text contrasts with selling ten dirhams from a lump of silver. Here, dividing the lump causes no harm, so the sale is valid. This helps identify the effective cause (illa): presence or absence of harm.
The illa is 'harm in delivery' – present in the beam/cloth cases, absent in the silver case.
4
Analyze the additional reason when the item is unspecified
If the beam or yard is not specifically identified within the larger object, the sale is invalid for two reasons: the harm mentioned above and ignorance (jahl) of the sold item, which renders the sale fasid.
When specified, only harm is the issue; when unspecified, both harm and ignorance apply.
5
Examine the exception and distinguish from hidden items
If the seller physically separates the item (cuts the yard or removes the beam) before the buyer cancels the sale, the sale becomes valid because the cause of invalidity (harm) is removed. However, this does not apply to hidden items like pits in dates or seeds in watermelon, because their existence is uncertain at the time of contract – such sales are void due to gharar even if extracted later.
The beam is a definite, visible entity, unlike hidden pits or seeds.

قال وجدع فى السقف وذراع من ثوب ذكرا القطع اولم يذكراه لانه لا يمكن تسليمه الا بضرر بخلاف ما اذا باع عشرة دراهم من نفرة فضة لانه لا ضرر فى تبعيضه ولو لم يكن معينا لا يجوز لماذ كرنا وللجهالة ايضا ولو قطع البائع الذراع او قلع الجذع قبل ان يفسخ المشترى يعود صحيحا لزوال المفسد بخلاف ما اذا باع النوى فى التمرا والبدر في البطيخ حيث لا يكون صحيحا وإن شقهما اخرج السيع لان في وجودهما احتمالا اما الجدع فعين موجود
ترجمہ اور شہتیر کی بیچ چھت میں اور کپڑے میں ایک گز کی بیع نا جائز ہے بائع اور مشتری دونوں نے کاٹنے کا ذکر کیا ہو یا کاٹنے کا ذکر نہ کیا ہو کیونکہ بغیر ضرر کے اس کو سپرد کرنا ممکن نہیں ہے۔ برخلاف اس کے جبکہ چاندی کے ٹکڑے میں سے دس درہم پھر چاندی فروخت کی ۔ کیونکہ اس کے ٹکڑے کرنے میں کوئی ضرر نہیں ہے۔ اور اگر معین نہ ہو تو بھی جائز نہیں ہے اس دلیل کی وجہ سے جو ہم نے ذکر کی اور جمیع مجہول ہونے کی وجہ سے اور اگر مشتری کے فتح کرنے سے پہلے بائع نے گڑ کاٹ دیا یا شہتیرا کھاڑ دیا تو بع عود کر کے صحیح ہو جائے گی ۔ کیونکہ فاسد کرنے والی چیز زائل ہو گئی ہے۔ برخلاف اس کے کہ اگر وہ گٹھلیاں فروخت کیں جو چھوہاروں میں ہیں یا وہ بیج فروخت کئے جو خربوزے کے اندر ہیں تو یہ بھی صحیح نہ ہوگی۔ اگر چہ بائع ان کو پھاڑ کر میچ کو نکال دے کیونکہ ان کے موجود ہونے میں احتمال ہے اور رہاشہتیر تو و محسوس اور موجود ہے۔
تشریح صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ شہتیر جو چھت میں ہو اس کا بیچنا جائز نہیں ہے اور کسی ایسے کپڑے سے ایک گز کا بیچنا جس سے کا بنا مصر ہو جائز نہیں ہے خواہ دونوں نے کاٹنے کی جگہ کا ذکر کیا ہو یا نہ کیا ہو کیونکہ بغیر ضرر کے بائع کیلئے اس کا سپر د کر نا ممکن نہیں ہے اور ضرر برداشت کرنا مقتضی معقد نہیں ہے اسلئے یہ بیچ درست نہ ہوگی ۔ ہاں اگر چاندی کے ڈھیلے میں سے دس درہم کے بقدر چاندی فروخت کی تو جائز ہے کیونکہ اس کے ٹکڑے کرنے میں کوئی ضرر نہیں ہے۔ اور اگر چھت کے اندر شہتیر اور کپڑے کے اندر گز متعین نہ ہو تو بیع دو وجہوں سے جائز نہیں ہے۔ ایک تو مذکورہ وجہ کی وجہ سے کہ بغیر ضرر کے بائع کیلئے بیع سپرد کرنا ممکن نہیں ہے ۔ دوم اسلئے کہ اس صورت میں مبیع جنہوں ۔ اور مبیع مجہول ہونے کی صورت میں بیع فاسد ہوتی ہے۔ اسلئے اس صورت میں بیع جائز نہ ہوگی ۔ اور اگر مشتری کے صبح کرنے سے پہلے بائع نے کپڑے سے ایک گر کاٹ دیا یا چھت سے ایک شہتیر اکھاڑ دیا تو یہ بیچ صحیح ہو جائے گی لیکن مفسد بیچ یعنی ضرر دور ہو گیا ہے ہاں اگر کسی نے چھوہاروں کے اندر کی گٹھلیاں یا خربوزے کے اندر بیج فروخت کئے تو یہ بیچ درست نہ ہوگی ۔ اگر چہ مشتری کے بیچ منع کرنے سے پہلے بائع نے چھوہاروں اور خربوزے کو پھاڑ کر مبیع یعنی گٹھلیاں اور بیج نکال لیا ہو کیونکہ فروخت کرتے وقت چونکہ گٹھلیاں اور بیج نظروں سے غائب تھے اسلئے ان کے وجود میں احتمال تھا کہ ہو سکتا ہے کہ ان کے اندر نہ ہوں یا ہوں تو خراب ہوں۔ پس اس صورت میں گو یا بیع با امیچ کے ہوئی اور با امبیع کے بیع باطل ہوتی ہے لہذا چھوہاروں کے اندر گٹھلیوں اور خربوزے کے اندریج کی
He said: And [it is not permissible to sell] a beam in the ceiling or a yard of cloth, whether they mention cutting or not, because it cannot be delivered without harm, unlike if he sold ten dirhams of a silver nugget because there is no harm in dividing it. If it is not specified, it is also not permissible for the reason we mentioned and due to ignorance. If the seller cuts the yard or removes the beam before the buyer cancels, the sale becomes valid because the invalidating factor is removed. Unlike if he sold pits in dates or seeds in a watermelon, where it is not valid even if he splits them and extracts the sold item because their existence is uncertain, but the beam is a definite entity. Translation: And selling a beam in the ceiling or a yard of cloth is not permissible, whether the seller and buyer mention cutting or not, because it cannot be delivered without harm. Unlike when he sells ten dirhams of a silver nugget, because there is no harm in dividing it. If it is not specified, it is also not permissible for the reason we mentioned and due to ignorance. And if the seller cuts the yard or removes the beam before the buyer cancels, the sale becomes valid because the invalidating factor is removed. Unlike if he sold pits that are in dates or seeds that are in a watermelon, then it is not valid even if he splits them and extracts the sold item because their existence is uncertain, but the beam is a definite and existing entity. Commentary: The issue is that selling a beam that is in a ceiling or selling a yard from a cloth that is stitched is not permissible, whether they mention the place of cutting or not, because it is not possible for the seller to deliver without causing harm, and bearing harm is not required by the contract. Therefore this sale is not valid. However, if he sells ten dirhams' worth of silver from a lump of silver, it is permissible because there is no harm in cutting it. And if the beam in the ceiling or the yard in the cloth is not specified, the sale is invalid for two reasons: the mentioned reason of harm, and because the sold item is unknown, which makes the sale void. And if before the buyer cancels, the seller cuts the yard or removes the beam from the ceiling, the sale becomes valid because the invalidating factor (harm) is removed. However, if someone sells the pits inside dates or seeds inside a watermelon, the sale is not valid even if the seller splits the fruit and extracts the sold item before cancellation, because at the time of sale their existence was uncertain; they might not be present or might be spoiled. So it is a sale with uncertainty, and such a sale is void. Therefore selling pits inside dates and seeds inside watermelons is invalid.
Source pages p. 169

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement with reasoning (talil). The matn states that selling a beam fixed in a ceiling or a specific yard of cloth from a piece of cloth is not permissible. The reason is that delivery would require causing harm (darar) to the remaining property (e.g., damaging the ceiling or cloth), and the contract does not oblige the seller to bear harm. This is contrasted with selling a specified amount of silver from a lump: there is no harm in cutting silver. If the beam or yard is not specified, the sale is additionally invalid due to ignorance (jahl) of the sold item. However, if the seller physically separates the sold item (cuts the yard or removes the beam) before the buyer exercises the option of cancellation (khiyar al-faskh), the sale becomes valid because the cause of invalidity (the harm) is removed. This is different from selling pits inside dates or seeds inside a watermelon: even if the seller extracts them before cancellation, the sale remains invalid because at the time of contract their existence was uncertain (there might be no pits or seeds, or they could be spoiled). This is a sale with gharar (uncertainty), which is void. The commentary emphasizes that the beam is a definite, visible entity, unlike hidden pits or seeds.

Key Terms
الجذع (al-jidh'): A beam fixed in a ceiling, sold separately from the ceiling.
الذراع (al-dhira'): A yard (unit of length) of cloth, sold as a specific portion from a larger piece.
ضرر (darar): Harm or damage caused to the remaining property by delivering the sold item.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What makes the sale of a yard of cloth from a stitched piece invalid according to the passage?
A) The cloth is not yet cut.
B) The delivery would cause harm to the remaining cloth.
C) The yard is not specifically identified.
D) The buyer does not intend to use it.

Key Takeaway
A sale of a part of a larger object is invalid if delivery necessarily harms the remainder, but becomes valid if the seller physically separates the part before the buyer cancels.

Buyu — Sales and Trade

8 min
Selling a Beam in the Ceiling and a Yard of Cloth
Ruling with proof on selling a fixed beam or a yard from cloth

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on selling a fixed beam or a yard of cloth and explain why the sale can become valid if the seller removes the item before rescission.

Core Idea
A sale that is fasid due to harm in delivery can be cured by removing the harm before rescission.

How can a sale that is initially invalid become valid? In this lesson, we examine a classic scenario: selling a beam fixed in a ceiling or a yard from a larger cloth. The Hanafi school rules these as fasid (irregular) because delivery requires harming the property. However, if the seller cuts or removes the item before the buyer exercises the right to rescind, the sale is corrected. This contrasts with selling date pits or melon seeds, which are batil (void) from the start.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and initial ruling
The act is selling a beam that is part of a ceiling or a yard from a cloth. The initial ruling is that the sale is not permissible (fasid). Why? Because the seller cannot deliver the item without causing harm (darar) to the remaining structure or cloth.
The ruling applies whether or not the cutting point is specified.
2
Locate the proof: analogy (qiyas jaliy)
The proof is based on qiyas: since delivery causes harm, it is analogous to other prohibited sales. The effective cause (illa) is the harm in delivery. This is contrasted with selling a portion of silver, where dividing causes no harm.
The illa is 'darar' (harm) – a key concept in Hanafi contracts.
3
Analyze the cure: removal of the mufsid
If the seller cuts the cloth or pulls out the beam before the buyer rescinds (faskh), the mufsid (invalidating factor) is removed. The sale then becomes valid (sahih) because the obstacle to delivery is gone.
This cure only works for fasid sales, not batil sales.
4
Distinguish from batil sales (date pits and melon seeds)
Selling date pits inside dates or melon seeds inside the fruit is batil (void), not fasid. Even if the seller extracts them, the sale remains invalid because at the time of contract the object was uncertain (non-existent or unknown). The beam and cloth are observable and existent; pits/seeds are not.
Thus, the ruling differs: fasid can be cured, batil cannot.
5
Determine the mufta bihi ruling
The operative ruling: such sales are invalid (fasid) until delivery becomes possible without harm. If the seller removes the item before rescission, it becomes valid. Otherwise, the buyer has the right to rescind.
This is from Zahir al-Riwayah and agreed upon by the three imams.

The ruling on selling a beam in the ceiling and a yard of cloth. He said: And the sale of a beam [fixed] in the ceiling and a yard of cloth – whether they mention cutting or not – is not permissible because its delivery is not possible without harm, unlike the case when one sells ten dirhams from a piece of silver, because there is no harm in dividing it. If it is not specified, it is also not permissible due to what we mentioned and due to ignorance. And if the seller cuts the yard or pulls out the beam before the buyer rescinds, the sale becomes valid because the invalidating factor is removed, unlike the case when one sells the pits in dates or the seeds in watermelon, where the sale is not valid even if he splits them and extracts the item, because there is possibility regarding their existence. But the beam is an existing entity.
Source pages p. 169

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the Hidayah on the sale of a beam fixed in a roof and a yard from a piece of cloth. The ruling is that such sales are invalid (fasid) because delivery cannot be made without causing harm to the structure or the remaining cloth. This is contrasted with selling a portion of a silver lump, where dividing causes no harm. The invalidity applies whether or not the cutting point is specified. If the item is not specified, the sale is also invalid due to ignorance (jahalah). However, if the seller actually cuts the cloth or removes the beam before the buyer exercises the option of rescission (khiyar al-faskh), the sale becomes valid because the obstacle (harm) is removed. This differs from selling date pits or melon seeds within the fruit, where the sale is batil (void) because the existence of the pits/seeds is uncertain (they may be absent or defective). Even if the seller extracts them, the sale remains invalid because at the time of contract the object was non-existent or unknown. Thus, the beam and cloth are observable existing items, so their sale is fasid (not batil) and can be corrected by removing the harm.

Key Terms
مفسد (mufsid): The invalidating factor that makes the sale fasid, here identified as 'harm' (ضرر) in delivery.
ضرر (darar): Harm that makes delivery impossible without damage to the property or remaining part.
فسخ (faskh): Rescission, the buyer's right to cancel a fasid sale before delivery.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The sale remains invalid because the initial contract was batil.
B) The sale becomes valid because the invalidating factor (harm) is removed.
C) The sale becomes valid only if the buyer agrees to pay more.
D) The sale becomes void because the object was not specified.

Key Takeaway
A sale that is fasid due to harm in delivery can be corrected by removing the harm before the buyer rescinds, distinguishing it from batil sales where the object is uncertain.

Selling the Catch of a Hunter's Net
Ruling on selling animals caught by a single net cast

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the sale of ضربة القانص is batil and state the two legal reasons (jahalah and gharar) for its prohibition.

Core Idea
A sale of uncertain catch is void because ignorance of the object invalidates the contract.

Islamic commercial law requires that the subject matter of a sale be known with certainty. When a hunter sells the catch of a net before it is drawn, the quantity and quality are unknown, and the sale may even yield harmful animals instead of game. This lesson examines the ruling on such a transaction and the underlying principles of jahalah (ignorance) and gharar (fraud).

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The act is the sale of ضربة القانص – the animals obtained by a single cast of a hunter's net. The ruling is that this sale is not permissible (ghayr ja'iz), i.e., void (batil).
2
Define the term ضربة القانص
Understand that it refers to an uncertain pool of animals: the hunter does not know how many or what creatures will be caught.
The term itself implies a single strike of the net.
3
Analyse the first reason: jahalah
The object of sale (mabi') is unknown (majhul). At the time of contract, the existence, quantity, and quality of the catch are all uncertain. This fundamental ignorance invalidates the sale.
A valid sale requires the object to be known (ma'lum) to both parties.
4
Analyse the second reason: gharar
There is fraud (gharar) because the net may catch harmful animals (snake, scorpion, dog) instead of game, making the transaction inherently deceptive.
Gharar is prohibited in sales as it leads to disputes.
5
Note the consequence
The sale is batil (void) ab initio; it cannot be rectified. Neither party acquires ownership or liability.
This ruling is unanimous among Hanafi imams.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ایک جال میں آنے والے جانوروں کی بیع کا حکم
قال وضربة القانص وهو ما يخرج من الصيد بضرب الشبكة مرة لانه مجهول ولان فيه غررا ترجمہ اور ضربتہ القانص کی بیع جائز نہیں ہے ضربقہ القانص وہ جانور جو ایک مرتبہ جال مارنے سے حاصل ہوں کیونکہ مبیع مجہول ہے اور اسلئے کہ اس میں دھوکہ ہے ۔ تشریح ضربة القانص وہ جانور جو ایک مرتبہ جال مارنے سے حاصل ہوں ضربة القائص کی بیچ اس لئے نا جائز ہے کہ اس صورت میں طبیع مجہول ہوتی ہے معلوم نہیں جال میں کتنے پرندے پھنسیں گے اور یہ بھی ہو سکتا ہے کہ کوئی پرندہ نہ پھنسے دوسری دلیل یہ ہے کہ اس بیچ میں دھوکہ ہے کیونکہ ہو سکتا ہے کہ جال میں شکار کے بجائے سانپ بچھو کتا پھنس جائے ۔
The ruling on selling animals that come into a net. He said: And ضربة القانص – which is what comes out of hunting by striking the net once – because it is unknown and because it involves deception. Translation: The sale of ضربة القانص is not permissible. ضربة القانص are the animals obtained by one net cast, because the object of sale is unknown and because there is fraud in it. Explanation: The sale of ضربة القانص is impermissible because the object of sale is unknown – one does not know how many birds will be caught, and it is possible that no bird is caught. The second proof is that there is fraud in this sale, because it is possible that instead of game, a snake, scorpion, or dog gets caught in the net.
Source pages p. 170

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement on the sale of ضربة القانص, defined as the catch obtained by a single cast of a hunter's net. The ruling is that such a sale is not permissible (ghayr ja'iz). The reasons given are: (1) the object of sale (mabi') is unknown (majhul) – the quantity and even existence of the catch is uncertain; (2) there is fraud (gharar) involved, as the net may catch harmful animals instead of game. This type of sale is therefore void (batil) due to jahalah and gharar, which are prohibited in Islamic commercial law. The commentary emphasizes that the uncertainty exists at the time of contract, making the sale invalid.

Key Terms
ضربة القانص (darbat al-qanis): The catch (usually birds or animals) obtained by a single cast of a hunter's net; an uncertain quantity/quality.
غرر (gharar): Fraud or excessive uncertainty that leads to risk, making the sale invalid.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) Because the hunter is not the owner
D) Because the animals are not halal

Key Takeaway
The sale of ضربة القانص is batil because the object is unknown and involves gharar, violating the fundamental requirement of certainty in the subject matter of a contract.

Muzabanah and Muhaqalah: Prohibition and 'Araya Exception
Ruling on Muzabanah and Muhaqalah with Shafi'i dispute on 'Araya

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on Muzabanah and Muhaqalah, explain the Shafi'i counter-argument, and apply the Hanafi interpretation of 'Araya as a gift to resolve the dispute.

Core Idea
Muzabanah is absolutely prohibited; the 'Araya exception is a gift, not a sale.

This passage addresses a key inter-madhhab dispute about the prohibition of Muzabanah (selling fresh fruit on trees for dried fruit by estimation) and Muhaqalah. The Hanafi school holds that these transactions are absolutely haram, while Imam al-Shafi'i argues for a limited exception under five wasqs based on the 'Araya concession. We will examine the Hanafi position, the Shafi'i proof, and the Hanafi linguistic rebuttal that reinterprets 'Araya as a gift transaction.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the ruling on Muzabanah and Muhaqalah: they are prohibited. Note the definitions: Muzabanah is selling fresh fruit on trees for dried fruit of the same type by estimation; Muhaqalah is selling wheat in ears for wheat by estimation.
The prohibition is based on a prophetic hadith and the principle that selling makil by estimation is invalid.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Imam al-Shafi'i argues that Muzabanah is permissible for less than five wasqs, citing the hadith that prohibits Muzabanah but permits 'Araya.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
The Shafi'i dalil is the hadith: 'The Prophet (SAW) prohibited Muzabanah but permitted 'Araya.' They interpret 'Araya as a sale of fresh dates for dried dates by estimation under five wasqs.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
The Hanafi school responds by analyzing the linguistic meaning of 'Araya: it means 'gift' in Arabic. The transaction is therefore a gift exchange, not a sale. The receiver sells the fruit back to the giver as a metaphorical sale (majaz) because the receiver never fully owned the fruit. Hence, it does not create an exception to the prohibition.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: Hanafi prohibits Muzabanah absolutely, even for small amounts; Shafi'i permits it under five wasqs. The mufta bihi in the Hanafi school is the absolute prohibition.
